Taharah — Purification

10 min
Specific Amounts of Water to Draw for Different Dead Animals in a Well
Ruling on required amounts of water to draw based on size of dead animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required amounts of water to draw from a well when a dead animal is found, identifying the obligatory and recommended portions for different animal sizes, and apply the Hanafi rulings to similar cases.

Core Idea
The amount of water to draw depends on the animal's size: 20 buckets for mouse-sized, 40 for pigeon-sized, all for sheep-sized; swelling changes the rule.

When a dead animal falls into a well, the water becomes impure to varying degrees. The Hanafi school prescribes specific amounts of water to be drawn based on the animal's body size, derived from prophetic hadith. This lesson will guide you through the classifications, the evidence, and the practical application of these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animal size category
For each category (mouse-like, pigeon-like, sheep-like), note the prescribed amount of water to draw.
Size is determined by body mass, not species.
2
Examine the dalil for each category
For mouse, hadith of Anas ibn Malik (20-30 buckets). For pigeon, hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (40-50 buckets). For sheep, fatwa of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Zubayr considered ijma (all water).
All ahadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah: obligation vs recommendation
The word 'aw' (or) in the hadith indicates that the lower number is certain (wajib), while the higher is recommended (mustahabb) to not abandon the narration.
This usul principle applies to all three scales.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf has a different calculation for multiple mice: for 1-4 mice, 20-30; for 5, 40-70; for 10, all. The standard view (matn) considers each mouse individually.
The mufta bihi is the standard view.
5
Apply special conditions: swelling/decomposition and alive vs dead
Swelling or decomposition overrides the size-based rule: all water must be drawn regardless of size. If the animal falls alive, impurity only occurs if its mouth touches the water (except for dog/pig).
These conditions are found in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعشرون دلواً وسطاً بموت نحو فارة، وأربعون بنحو حمامة، وكله بنحو شاة وانتفاخ حيوان أو تفسخه. بموت نحو فارة : المراد بنحو الفارة ما يكون مثلها أو قاربها في الجثة كالعصفور والصعوة والسودانية وسام أبرص، ونزح عشرين دلوا بعد إخراج نحو الفارة، فلو نزح قبل إخراجها فلا تطهر، وإخراج عشرين لما روى أنس بن مالك عن النبي أنه قال في الفارة: 'إذا ماتت في البئر: إنه ينزح منها عشرون دلواً وسطاً أو ثلاثون'، وكلمة 'أو' لأحد الشيئين، فكان الأقل ثابتاً بيقين، والأكثر يؤتى به كيلا يترك اللفظ المروي، وإن كان مستغنى عنه في العمل، وهو معنى الاستحباب، وإنما قيد بالموت؛ لأنه لو أخرج ما وقع فيه حياً لا يتنجس إلا في الكلب والخنزير، وفي غيرهما ينظر إن أصاب فمه الماء وسؤره نجس فالماء نجس، وإن كان سؤره مكروهاً فالماء مكروه، وإن كان مشكوكاً فمشكوك، ينزع ماء البئر كله، وإن لم يصب فمه الماء لا ينزح شيء، وعند أبي يوسف: ينزح عشرون إلى ثلاثين في الفارة الواحدة، وكذلك إلى الأربع، وإن كانت خمسا ينزح أربعون إلى سبعين، وإن كانت عشراً فالجميع. (مستخلص ومسكين ونهاية) فارة كعصفور وصعوة، والفارتان كفارة، والثلاثة كالدجاجة، والست كالشاة وهو الصحيح. وأربعون أي ينزح أربعون دلواً وسطاً بنحو حمامة في الجسد كالدجاجة والسنور؛ لما روي عن أبي سعيد الخدري أنه قال في الدجاجة إذا ماتت في البئر : ينزح منها أربعون دلواً، وفي الجامع الصغير': أربعون أو خمسون دلوا، والأول لبيان الإيجاب، والثاني لبيان الاستحباب، والدلو الوسط قيل: هو أن يسع فيه صاع، والأصغر ما دون الصاع، والأكبر ما فوق الصاع، والصحيح المعتبر دلو تلك البئر، ولو نزح بدلو عظيم يسع العشرين أو الأربعين مرة واحدة جاز؛ الحصول المقصود ولا يشترط في الدلاء كونها مملوءة، بل يكفي ملأ أكثرها، والدلو الأصغر والأكبر يحاسب بالوسط. (فتح ومستخلص وغيره) بنحو حمامة كدجاجة وسنور وجوباً وخمسون استحباباً. وكله أي يجب نزح كل ماء البئر بموت شاة ونحوها في الجسد كآدمي وكلب؛ لأن ابن عباس وابن زبير من أفتيا بنزح كل الماء حين مات زنجي في بئر زمزم من غير نكير فكان إجماعاً. (فتح المعين) وانتفاخ حيوان إلخ: ينزح الماء كله بانتفاخ حيوان أو تفسخه فيه، سواء كان الحيوان صغيراً أو كبيراً، ولا يجب نزح الطين لمكان الحرج، بل يجب نزح كل الماء لانتشار البلة في أجزاء الماء؛ لأن هذا الانتفاخ والتفسخ ينفصل
And twenty medium buckets by the death of something like a mouse, and forty buckets by something like a pigeon, and all (water) by something like a sheep and by the swelling of an animal or its decomposition. 'By the death of something like a mouse': what is meant by something like a mouse is what is like it or similar in body such as a sparrow, a small bird, a black bird, and a gecko. And twenty buckets are drawn after removing the mouse-like animal. If he draws before removing it, it does not become pure. The drawing of twenty is due to what Anas ibn Malik narrated from the Prophet that he said regarding a mouse: 'If it dies in the well, twenty or thirty medium buckets are drawn from it.' The word 'or' indicates one of two things, so the smaller is established with certainty, and the larger is brought so as not to leave the narrated wording, even if it is unnecessary in practice, and that is the meaning of recommendation (istihbab). And it is restricted to death because if it falls in alive, it does not become impure except for dog and pig. In other cases, it is considered: if its mouth hits the water and its leftover is impure, then the water is impure; if its leftover is disliked, then the water is disliked; if it is doubtful, then doubtful. All water of the well is drawn. And if its mouth does not hit the water, nothing is drawn. According to Abu Yusuf: twenty to thirty are drawn for one mouse, similarly up to four; if five, forty to seventy; if ten, all. (Mustakhlas, Miskeen, Nihaya) A mouse is like a sparrow and a small bird; two mice like one mouse; three like a chicken; six like a sheep; that is the correct view. 'And forty' i.e. forty medium buckets are drawn by something like a pigeon in body, like a chicken and a cat, because of what is narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that he said regarding a chicken dying in the well: forty buckets are drawn from it. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: forty or fifty buckets; the first indicates obligation (ijab), the second recommendation (istihbab). The medium bucket is said to hold a sa'. The smaller is less than a sa', the larger more. The correct view is to consider the bucket of that well. If he draws with a huge bucket that holds twenty or forty at once, it is permissible, because the purpose is achieved. It is not required that the buckets be full; it is sufficient that most of them are full. The smaller and larger buckets are calculated as medium. (Fath, Mustakhlas, etc.) 'By something like a pigeon' like a chicken and a cat, obligatory, and fifty is recommended. 'And all' i.e. all water of the well must be drawn by the death of a sheep and similar in body like a human and a dog, because Ibn Abbas and Ibn Zubayr gave a fatwa to draw all water when a black man died in the well of Zamzam without any objection, so it was consensus. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Swelling of an animal etc.': all water is drawn by the swelling of an animal or its decomposition in the well, whether the animal is small or large. It is not obligatory to draw the mud due to hardship, but all water must be drawn because the moisture spreads in the water, as this swelling and decomposition separates.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on the amount of water to be drawn from a well when a dead animal falls into it, classified by the size of the animal. The matn states: twenty medium buckets for something like a mouse, forty for something like a pigeon, and all water for something like a sheep, as well as for any animal that swells or decomposes. The commentator first explains that 'something like a mouse' includes small creatures like sparrows, geckos, etc. The proof is from the hadith of Anas from the Prophet (SAW) that for a mouse, twenty or thirty buckets are drawn; the lower number is obligatory, the higher is recommended. The commentator also discusses the scenario if the animal falls alive: only dog and pig cause impurity; for others, consider if the mouth touched the water. Note the difference of Abu Yusuf regarding multiple mice. Then for a pigeon-sized animal (like chicken, cat), forty is obligatory, fifty recommended, proven by the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. For a sheep-sized animal (including human, dog), all water must be drawn, based on the fatwa of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Zubayr regarding a black man in Zamzam, considered Ijma. Finally, if an animal swells or decomposes, all water is drawn regardless of size, because the impurity spreads throughout the water. Mud need not be removed due to hardship.

Key Terms
دلو (dalw): Bucket used for drawing water. Medium bucket (wasat) is defined as holding a sa'.
فارة (fārah): Mouse; used as a standard for small creatures.
حمامة (ḥamāmah): Pigeon; used as a standard for medium-sized animals like chicken and cat.
شاة (shāh): Sheep/goat; used as a standard for large animals including human and dog.
انتفاخ (intifākh): Swelling of a dead animal in water.
تفسخ (tafasukh): Decomposition of a dead animal in water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 20 buckets
B) 40 buckets
C) All water
D) 50 buckets

Key Takeaway
The required amount of water to draw from a well depends on the size of the dead animal, with obligatory minimums and recommended additional amounts based on prophetic hadith.

Urine of Halal-Meat Animals: Najasah and Consumption
Expansion on the ruling of urine consumption and garment impurity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the urine of halal-meat animals and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a garment impurity scenario.

Core Idea
Urine of halal animals is najis (Abu Hanifa); but Muhammad says tahir, Abu Yusuf najis but drinkable for medicine.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a practical issue: the urine of animals we commonly eat, like sheep and chickens. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement, but the relied-upon position follows Abu Hanifa. We will examine the three views and their consequences for drinking and clothing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the urine of animals whose meat is eaten. The matn states it is not drunk at all. Determine the hukm level: haram (according to Abu Hanifa) or permissible (according to Muhammad)?
The hukm depends on the school's ruling on najasah.
2
Map the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
State the three positions: Abu Hanifa: najis, no drinking even for medicine; Muhammad: tahir, drinkable; Abu Yusuf: najis but drinkable for medicine.
This is an example of ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Apply the ruling to garments
The text gives the effect on clothing: Muhammad says no impurity; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say it makes the garment impure unless the amount is small (quarter of the area or a handspan).
The mufta bihi is that it is najis, so clothes must be washed unless the amount is negligible.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Abu Hanifa's view: urine of halal animals is najis, cannot be drunk, and makes clothing impure unless very little.
Tarjih authority: Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.

Source Text

أحكام البئر
ولا يشرب أصلا، وعشرون دلواً وسطاً بموت نحو فارة، وأربعون بنحو حمامة، أي وينزح وكله بنحو شاة وانتفاخ حيوان أو تفسخه. فكان كدم البعوض والدماء التي تبقى في العروق. (مسكين، فتح المعين) ولا يشرب أصلا أي بول ما يؤكل لحمه أصلا في حال من الأحوال ولا تداوياً عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن التداوي بالطاهر الحرام كلبن الأتان لا يجوز فما ظنك بالنجس وعند محمد: يشرب للتداوي وغيره لطهارته عنده، وعند أبي يوسف: يشرب للتداوي ولا يجوز لغيره، ولو أصاب الثوب لا ينجسه عند محمد وتجوز الصلاة فيه وإن امتلأ بالثوب منه، وعلى قولهما ينجس الثوب، إلا أنه يجوز الصلاة فيه ما لم يكن كثيراً فاحشا وهو ربع الموضع الذي أصابه كالذيل، وعند أبي يوسف شبر في شبر. (ملا مسكين) بموت نحو فارة : المراد بنحو الفارة ما يكون مثلها أو قاربها في الجثة كالعصفور والصعوة والسودانية وسام أبرص، ونزح عشرين دلوا بعد إخراج نحو الفارة، فلو نزح قبل إخراجها فلا تطهر، وإخراج عشرين لما روى أنس بن مالك عن النبي أنه قال في الفارة: "إذا ماتت في البئر: إنه ينزح منها عشرون دلواً وسطاً أو ثلاثون"، وكلمة "أو" لأحد الشيئين، فكان الأقل ثابتاً بيقين، والأكثر يؤتى به كيلا يترك اللفظ المروي، وإن كان مستغنى عنه في العمل، وهو معنى الاستحباب، وإنما قيد بالموت؛ لأنه لو أخرج ما وقع فيه حياً لا يتنجس إلا في الكلب والخنزير، وفي غيرهما ينظر إن أصاب فمه الماء وسؤره نجس فالماء نجس، وإن كان سؤره مكروهاً فالماء مكروه، وإن كان مشكوكاً فمشكوك، ينزح ماء البئر كله، وإن لم يصب فمه الماء لا ينزح شيء، وعند أبي يوسف: ينزح عشرون إلى ثلاثين في الفارة الواحدة، وكذلك إلى الأربع، وإن كانت خمسا ينزح أربعون إلى سبعين، وإن كانت عشراً فالجميع. (مستخلص ومسكين ونهاية فارة كعصفور وصعوة، والفارتان كفارة، والثلاثة كالدجاجة، والست كالشاة وهو الصحيح. وأربعون أي ينزح أربعون دلواً وسطاً بنحو حمامة في الجسد كالدجاجة والسنور؛ لما روي عن أبي سعيد الخدري أنه قال في الدجاجة إذا ماتت في البئر : ينزح منها أربعون دلواً، وفي الجامع الصغير": أربعون أو خمسون دلوا، والأول لبيان الإيجاب، والثاني لبيان الاستحباب، والدلو الوسط قيل: هو أن يسع فيه صاع، والأصغر ما دون الصاع، والأكبر ما فوق الصاع، والصحيح المعتبر دلو تلك البئر، ولو نزح بدلو عظيم يسع العشرين أو الأربعين مرة واحدة جاز؛ الحصول المقصود ولا يشترط في الدلاء كونها مملوءة، بل يكفي ملأ أكثرها، والدلو الأصغر والأكبر يحاسب بالوسط. (فتح ومستخلص وغيره) بنحو حمامة كدجاجة وسنور وجوباً وخمسون استحباباً. وكله أي يجب نزح كل ماء البئر بموت شاة ونحوها في الجسد كآدمي وكلب؛ لأن ابن عباس وابن زبير من أفتيا بنزح كل الماء حين مات زنجي في بئر زمزم من غير نكير فكان إجماعاً.
Book of Purification. Chapter of the Well. And it is not drunk at all, and twenty medium buckets for the death of something like a mouse, and forty for something like a pigeon, meaning all water is drawn for something like a sheep and swelling or disintegration of an animal. So it is like the blood of mosquitoes and blood that remains in veins. (Miskin, Fath al-Mu'in): 'And it is not drunk at all' meaning the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten is not drunk at all in any situation and not for medicine according to Abu Hanifa; because treatment with permissible but forbidden things like donkey's milk is not permissible, so what do you think about impurity? According to Muhammad: it is drunk for medicine and otherwise because it is pure according to him. According to Abu Yusuf: it is drunk for medicine and not permissible for other purposes. And if it hits the garment, it does not make it impure according to Muhammad, and prayer is permissible in it even if the garment is filled with it. According to the two of them, it makes the garment impure, but prayer is permissible in it as long as it is not excessively abundant, which is a quarter of the area it hit like the hem, and according to Abu Yusuf a handspan by a handspan. (Mulla Miskin): By the death of something like a mouse: meant by 'like a mouse' is what is similar to it or close in body size, like a sparrow, a small bird, a black beetle, and a gecko. And drawing twenty buckets after removing the mouse; if drawn before removing it, the well does not become pure. And the drawing of twenty is due to what Anas ibn Malik narrated from the Prophet: concerning the mouse: 'If it dies in the well, twenty medium buckets or thirty are drawn from it.' The word 'or' indicates one of two things, so the lesser is established with certainty, and the greater is brought so as not to leave the narrated word, even if it is unnecessary in practice, and that is the meaning of recommendation. And it is restricted to death because if it falls in alive, the water does not become impure except in the case of a dog and pig. In other than these, if its mouth touched the water and its leftover water is impure, then the water is impure; if its leftover water is disliked, then the water is disliked; if doubtful, then doubtful, and all the well water is drawn. And if its mouth did not touch the water, nothing is drawn. According to Abu Yusuf: twenty to thirty buckets for one mouse, and so up to four; if there are five, forty to seventy buckets; if there are ten, all the water. (Mustakhlas, Miskin, and Nihaya): A mouse like a sparrow and a small bird; two mice like one mouse; three like a chicken; six like a sheep, and that is correct. And forty: meaning forty medium buckets are drawn for something like a pigeon in body, like a chicken and a cat; because it is narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that he said concerning a chicken that dies in a well: forty buckets are drawn from it. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: forty or fifty buckets; the first indicates obligation, the second recommendation. The medium bucket is said to be one sa' capacity; the smaller is less than a sa', the larger is more. The correct view is the bucket of that well. And if one draws with a huge bucket equal to twenty or forty at once, it is permissible because the purpose is achieved; it is not necessary that the buckets be full, rather filling most of them is sufficient, and the smaller and larger buckets are calculated as medium. (Fath, Mustakhlas, etc.): For something like a pigeon, like a chicken and a cat, forty is obligatory and fifty recommended. And 'all of it' means all the well water must be drawn upon the death of a sheep and similar in body, like a human and a dog; because Ibn Abbas and Ibn Zubayr gave a fatwa to draw all the water when a black man died in the well of Zamzam without any objection, so it was consensus.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof addressing two issues: the urine of animals whose meat is eaten, and the purification of a well when a small animal dies in it. The matn begins with the statement that such urine is not to be drunk at all, and then transitions to the well rulings. The commentary explains that according to Abu Hanifa, the urine of halal meat animals is impure (najis) and cannot be consumed even for medicinal purposes. Imam Muhammad considers it pure, while Abu Yusuf permits it only for medicine. Regarding the well, the Prophet reported by Anas ibn Malik prescribed twenty or thirty buckets for a mouse; the lesser number is obligatory, the greater recommended. The animal must be removed before drawing the water. For a pigeon-sized animal, forty buckets are obligatory, fifty recommended. If the animal is as large as a sheep, all the water must be drawn, as established by the practice of the Companions at Zamzam. The well is purified by drawing water according to these amounts.

Key Terms
بول ما يؤكل لحمه (bawl ma' yu'kalu lahmuhu): Urine of animals whose meat is permissible to eat, such as sheep, cows, chickens.
ربع الموضع (rub' al-mawdi'): Quarter of the area that the urine touches on the garment; if less, it is excused.
شبر (shibr): A handspan, approximately 20-25 cm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on drinking the urine of a sheep for medicinal purposes?
A) Permissible because it is pure according to Muhammad.
B) Permissible only for medicine according to Abu Yusuf.
C) Not permissible under any circumstances.
D) Permissible if mixed with water.

Key Takeaway
The urine of halal-meat animals is najis (mufta bihi), cannot be drunk, and a small amount on garments is excused.

Well Purification for Small Animals: Required Buckets
Detailed ruling on well purification amounts with proof and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the number of buckets required to purify a well when a small animal dies in it, apply conditions for valid purification, and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Twenty medium buckets for a mouse, forty for a pigeon, all water for a sheep — each based on hadith and consensus.

When a mouse, pigeon, or similar animal dies in a well, the water becomes impure. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq gives the exact numbers of buckets to draw, based on the Prophet's hadith and the Companions' practice. We will learn the amounts, the condition of removing the animal first, and the definition of a medium bucket.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animal and its size category
Animals are grouped by body size: mouse/sparrow (20 buckets), pigeon/chicken (40 buckets), sheep/human (all water).
The text gives categories: 'like a mouse' includes sparrow, gecko; 'like a pigeon' includes chicken, cat; 'like a sheep' includes human, dog.
2
Apply the hadith proof for the mouse
The hadith of Anas ibn Malik states: 20 or 30 buckets. The Hanafi principle: the lower number is obligatory (wajib), the higher is recommended.
The imperative 'ينزح' indicates obligation.
3
Check the condition of removing the animal first
The animal must be removed before drawing water; drawing before removal does not purify the well.
If the animal is removed alive, the well does not become impure except for dog and pig.
4
Determine the medium bucket
The medium bucket is defined by the well's own bucket; if a huge bucket is used that equals the total volume once, it suffices.
No need for the bucket to be full; most of its capacity is enough.
5
Apply the consensus for sheep-sized animals
When a sheep or human dies in the well, all water must be drawn, based on the Companions' fatwa on the Zamzam well.
This is considered ijma' (consensus).

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة
۲۸
أحكام البئر
ولا يشرب أصلا، وعشرون دلواً وسطاً بموت نحو فارة، وأربعون بنحو حمامة، أي وينزح وكله بنحو شاة وانتفاخ حيوان أو تفسخه. فكان كدم البعوض والدماء التي تبقى في العروق. (مسكين، فتح المعين) ولا يشرب أصلا أي بول ما يؤكل لحمه أصلا في حال من الأحوال ولا تداوياً عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن التداوي بالطاهر الحرام كلبن الأتان لا يجوز فما ظنك بالنجس وعند محمد: يشرب للتداوي وغيره لطهارته عنده، وعند أبي يوسف: يشرب للتداوي ولا يجوز لغيره، ولو أصاب الثوب لا ينجسه عند محمد وتجوز الصلاة فيه وإن امتلأ بالثوب منه، وعلى قولهما ينجس الثوب، إلا أنه يجوز الصلاة فيه ما لم يكن كثيراً فاحشا وهو ربع الموضع الذي أصابه كالذيل، وعند أبي يوسف شبر في شبر. (ملا مسكين) بموت نحو فارة : المراد بنحو الفارة ما يكون مثلها أو قاربها في الجثة كالعصفور والصعوة والسودانية وسام أبرص، ونزح عشرين دلوا بعد إخراج نحو الفارة، فلو نزح قبل إخراجها فلا تطهر، وإخراج عشرين لما روى أنس بن مالك عن النبي أنه قال في الفارة: "إذا ماتت في البئر: إنه ينزح منها عشرون دلواً وسطاً أو ثلاثون"، وكلمة "أو" لأحد الشيئين، فكان الأقل ثابتاً بيقين، والأكثر يؤتى به كيلا يترك اللفظ المروي، وإن كان مستغنى عنه في العمل، وهو معنى الاستحباب، وإنما قيد بالموت؛ لأنه لو أخرج ما وقع فيه حياً لا يتنجس إلا في الكلب والخنزير، وفي غيرهما ينظر إن أصاب فمه الماء وسؤره نجس فالماء نجس، وإن كان سؤره مكروهاً فالماء مكروه، وإن كان مشكوكاً فمشكوك، ينزح ماء البئر كله، وإن لم يصب فمه الماء لا ينزح شيء، وعند أبي يوسف: ينزح عشرون إلى ثلاثين في الفارة الواحدة، وكذلك إلى الأربع، وإن كانت خمسا ينزح أربعون إلى سبعين، وإن كانت عشراً فالجميع. (مستخلص ومسكين ونهاية فارة كعصفور وصعوة، والفارتان كفارة، والثلاثة كالدجاجة، والست كالشاة وهو الصحيح. وأربعون أي ينزح أربعون دلواً وسطاً بنحو حمامة في الجسد كالدجاجة والسنور؛ لما روي عن أبي سعيد الخدري أنه قال في الدجاجة إذا ماتت في البئر : ينزح منها أربعون دلواً، وفي الجامع الصغير": أربعون أو خمسون دلوا، والأول لبيان الإيجاب، والثاني لبيان الاستحباب، والدلو الوسط قيل: هو أن يسع فيه صاع، والأصغر ما دون الصاع، والأكبر ما فوق الصاع، والصحيح المعتبر دلو تلك البئر، ولو نزح بدلو عظيم يسع العشرين أو الأربعين مرة واحدة جاز؛ الحصول المقصود ولا يشترط في الدلاء كونها مملوءة، بل يكفي ملأ أكثرها، والدلو الأصغر والأكبر يحاسب بالوسط. (فتح ومستخلص وغيره) بنحو حمامة كدجاجة وسنور وجوباً وخمسون استحباباً. وكله أي يجب نزح كل ماء البئر بموت شاة ونحوها في الجسد كآدمي وكلب؛ لأن ابن عباس وابن زبير من أفتيا بنزح كل الماء حين مات زنجي في بئر زمزم من غير نكير فكان إجماعاً.
Book of Purification. Chapter of the Well. And it is not drunk at all, and twenty medium buckets for the death of something like a mouse, and forty for something like a pigeon, meaning all water is drawn for something like a sheep and swelling or disintegration of an animal. So it is like the blood of mosquitoes and blood that remains in veins. (Miskin, Fath al-Mu'in): 'And it is not drunk at all' meaning the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten is not drunk at all in any situation and not for medicine according to Abu Hanifa; because treatment with permissible but forbidden things like donkey's milk is not permissible, so what do you think about impurity? According to Muhammad: it is drunk for medicine and otherwise because it is pure according to him. According to Abu Yusuf: it is drunk for medicine and not permissible for other purposes. And if it hits the garment, it does not make it impure according to Muhammad, and prayer is permissible in it even if the garment is filled with it. According to the two of them, it makes the garment impure, but prayer is permissible in it as long as it is not excessively abundant, which is a quarter of the area it hit like the hem, and according to Abu Yusuf a handspan by a handspan. (Mulla Miskin): By the death of something like a mouse: meant by 'like a mouse' is what is similar to it or close in body size, like a sparrow, a small bird, a black beetle, and a gecko. And drawing twenty buckets after removing the mouse; if drawn before removing it, the well does not become pure. And the drawing of twenty is due to what Anas ibn Malik narrated from the Prophet: concerning the mouse: 'If it dies in the well, twenty medium buckets or thirty are drawn from it.' The word 'or' indicates one of two things, so the lesser is established with certainty, and the greater is brought so as not to leave the narrated word, even if it is unnecessary in practice, and that is the meaning of recommendation. And it is restricted to death because if it falls in alive, the water does not become impure except in the case of a dog and pig. In other than these, if its mouth touched the water and its leftover water is impure, then the water is impure; if its leftover water is disliked, then the water is disliked; if doubtful, then doubtful, and all the well water is drawn. And if its mouth did not touch the water, nothing is drawn. According to Abu Yusuf: twenty to thirty buckets for one mouse, and so up to four; if there are five, forty to seventy buckets; if there are ten, all the water. (Mustakhlas, Miskin, and Nihaya): A mouse like a sparrow and a small bird; two mice like one mouse; three like a chicken; six like a sheep, and that is correct. And forty: meaning forty medium buckets are drawn for something like a pigeon in body, like a chicken and a cat; because it is narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that he said concerning a chicken that dies in a well: forty buckets are drawn from it. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: forty or fifty buckets; the first indicates obligation, the second recommendation. The medium bucket is said to be one sa' capacity; the smaller is less than a sa', the larger is more. The correct view is the bucket of that well. And if one draws with a huge bucket equal to twenty or forty at once, it is permissible because the purpose is achieved; it is not necessary that the buckets be full, rather filling most of them is sufficient, and the smaller and larger buckets are calculated as medium. (Fath, Mustakhlas, etc.): For something like a pigeon, like a chicken and a cat, forty is obligatory and fifty recommended. And 'all of it' means all the well water must be drawn upon the death of a sheep and similar in body, like a human and a dog; because Ibn Abbas and Ibn Zubayr gave a fatwa to draw all the water when a black man died in the well of Zamzam without any objection, so it was consensus.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof addressing two issues: the urine of animals whose meat is eaten, and the purification of a well when a small animal dies in it. The matn begins with the statement that such urine is not to be drunk at all, and then transitions to the well rulings. The commentary explains that according to Abu Hanifa, the urine of halal meat animals is impure (najis) and cannot be consumed even for medicinal purposes. Imam Muhammad considers it pure, while Abu Yusuf permits it only for medicine. Regarding the well, the Prophet reported by Anas ibn Malik prescribed twenty or thirty buckets for a mouse; the lesser number is obligatory, the greater recommended. The animal must be removed before drawing the water. For a pigeon-sized animal, forty buckets are obligatory, fifty recommended. If the animal is as large as a sheep, all the water must be drawn, as established by the practice of the Companions at Zamzam. The well is purified by drawing water according to these amounts.

Key Terms
نزح (nazh): Drawing water from the well for purification.
دلو وسط (dalw wasat): A medium-sized bucket; the correct view is the bucket customarily used for that well.
نحو فارة (nahw fa'ra): Something like a mouse in body size, including sparrow, small bird, black beetle, gecko.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many medium buckets are wajib when a pigeon dies in a well?
A) 20
B) 30
C) 40
D) All water

Key Takeaway
The number of buckets required to purify a well depends on the size of the dead animal: 20 for mouse-sized, 40 for pigeon-sized, all water for sheep-sized.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Drawing All Water When an Animal Swells or Decomposes
Ruling on full nazh due to swelling/decomposition with definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that all water must be drawn when an animal swells or decomposes in a well, distinguish between intifakh and takhsukh, and explain the evidentiary basis in consensus (ijma).

Core Idea
Swelling or decomposition releases liquid impurity that permeates all the water, making full nazh wajib.

This lesson addresses a critical taharah rule: what happens if a dead animal in a well shows signs of swelling or decomposition. Unlike a fresh carcass where a fixed number of buckets suffices, here the impurity is considered to have spread throughout the water, requiring complete removal. We will explore the precise definitions of these conditions and the consensus (ijma) that supports this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
Note that the ruling applies specifically when the animal has swollen (intifakh) or disintegrated (takhsukh). The size of the animal is irrelevant.
The condition is independent of the animal's original size.
2
Understand the definitions
Intifakh is swelling so that hair or feathers fall off with gentle touch. Takhsukh is disintegration of the body after death. Both release liquid impurity (like drops of wine or urine) that spreads through the water.
The commentary from al-Mustakhlas makes this distinction.
3
Recognize the evidentiary basis
The ruling is supported by the consensus (ijma) of the Companions, as narrated from the incident at Zamzam where a black man died in the well and they ordered all water to be drawn. Their silence on the matter indicates acceptance.
The dalil is qati' al-thubut (definitive transmission) but zanni al-dalalah (interpretive meaning).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(فتح المعين) وانتفاخ حيوان إلخ: ينزح الماء كله بانتفاخ حيوان أو تفسخه فيه، سواء كان الحيوان صغيراً أو كبيراً، ولا يجب نزح الطين لمكان الحرج، بل يجب نزح كل الماء لانتشار البلة في أجزاء الماء؛ لأن هذا الانتفاخ والتفسخ ينفصل منها بلة، وتلك البلة نجاسة مائعة بمنزلة القطر من الخمر أو البول، كذا في "المستخلص". والفرق بين الانتفاخ والتفسخ أن الانتفاخ تورم في جسد الميت بحيث لو مسح جلده بإصبع أو حطب بالرفق لزال شعره وريشه، والتفسخ : أن يتمعط أجزاء الميت ويتفرق كلها أو بعضها بعد الموت. (محشي) ومائتان إلخ: عدم إمكان النزح إذا كانت البئر معينة أي جارية، فعند محمد ينزح مائتا دلو إلى ثلاث مائة، وعند أبي يوسف يخرج مقدار ما كان فيها من الماء، وطريق معرفته أن يؤخذ بقول رجلين لهما بصارة في أمور الماء، وهذا أشبه بالفقه (مسكين ملخصاً) ونجسها إلخ ماض من التنجيس، يعني إذا وجد في البئر فارة أو نحوها و لم يدر متى وقعت وقد انتفخت أو تفسخت ينجس البئر مذ ثلاثة أيام ولياليها، يعني أعادوا صلاة هذه الأيام، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : ليس عليهم إعادة شيء حتى يحققوا متى وقعت. (مسكين وغيره) وقت وقوعها بالرفع فاعل "جهل"، ثم التقدير بثلاث مذهب الإمام؛ لأن وقوع الحيوان الدموي في الماء لموته لاسيما في البئر، وزمان الوقوع سابق على زمان الوجود، فقدر بثلاثة أيام؛ لأنه لا ينتفخ إلا بعد ثلاثة أيام، وأبو يوسف كان يقول بقول أبي حنيفة إلى أن رأى حداءة في منقارها جيفة، فطرحتها في بئر فرجع عن قوله، والمفتى به قولهما، أي يتنجس مذ وجد إلا أن يعلم وقتها. (فتح) وإلا مذ يوم أي وإن لم تكن منتفخة أو متفسخة نجسها مذ يوم وليلة عنده، خلافاً لهما.
(Fath al-Mu'in): Swelling of an animal etc.: All water is drawn if an animal swells or decomposes in it, whether the animal is small or large. Mud does not have to be removed due to hardship, but all water must be removed because moisture spreads through the water; this swelling and disintegration release moisture, and that moisture is liquid impurity like drops of wine or urine. This is in al-Mustakhlas. The difference between swelling (intifakh) and disintegration (takhsukh) is that swelling is inflation of the body where if you wipe its skin with a finger or wood gently, its hair or feathers fall off. Disintegration is that the parts of the dead body become loose and separate entirely or partially after death. (Hashiyah): The 200 buckets etc.: When nazh is impossible, if the well is flowing (ma'in), according to Muhammad, 200 to 300 buckets are drawn; according to Abu Yusuf, the amount of water originally in the well is removed, and this is determined by the opinion of two experts in water matters. This is more in line with fiqh. (Miskin summarized): 'And its becoming impure' etc. is the past tense of tanjis, meaning if a mouse or similar is found in the well and it is not known when it fell, and it is swollen or decomposed, the well becomes impure from three days and nights ago; meaning they repeat the prayers of these days. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two say: they do not have to repeat anything until they ascertain when it fell. (Miskin and others): 'The time of its fall' in the nominative as the subject of 'unknown'; then the estimation is of three days according to the Imam, because the falling of a blood-containing animal into water leads to its death, especially in a well, and the time of falling precedes the time of discovery, so it is estimated at three days because it does not swell except after three days. Abu Yusuf used to follow Abu Hanifa until he saw a kite with a carcass in its beak, which it dropped into a well, so he retracted his opinion. The fatwa is given on their (the two's) opinion: that it becomes impure from the time it is found unless its time is known. (Fath): 'And otherwise' meaning if it is not swollen or decomposed, it becomes impure from one day and night according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to the two.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage continues the well rulings, focusing on cases where the animal has swollen or decomposed. The matn states that all water must be drawn if the animal shows these signs, regardless of its original size. The commentary explains that swelling (intifakh) and disintegration (takhsukh) release liquid impurity throughout the water. A distinction is made: in swelling, the skin loses hair/feathers easily; in disintegration, parts separate. If full nazh is impossible (e.g., a flowing well), Muhammad prescribes 200-300 buckets, while Abu Yusuf says to estimate the original water volume by expert witnesses. For unknown time of fall, Abu Hanifa retroactively applies impurity to three days if swollen/decomposed (since swelling takes 3 days), and one day if not. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say no retroactive impurity unless time is known. Abu Yusuf originally agreed with Abu Hanifa but later recanted when he saw a kite dropping a carcass into a well. The mufta bihi is the opinion of the two: the well is impure from the time the carcass is found, not retroactively.

Key Terms
انتفاخ (intifakh): Swelling of a dead animal's body such that hair/feathers fall off when gently touched.
تفسخ (takhsukh): Disintegration of the dead animal's body, parts separating after death.
بئر معينة (bi'r mu'ayyanah): A flowing well (i.e., not a static well). When nazh is impossible, special rules apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what triggers the obligation to draw all water from a well when a dead animal is found?
A) The animal must be large (e.g., a cat or larger).
B) The animal must have been dead for more than three days.
C) The animal shows signs of intifakh (swelling) or takhsukh (disintegration).
D) The animal is a blood-containing animal regardless of its condition.

Key Takeaway
Swelling or decomposition of a dead animal in a well releases liquid impurity that requires complete removal of all water (full nazh), even if the animal is small.

Taharah — Purification

When Full Nazh Is Impossible: Flowing Wells and Expert Estimation
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on method when full nazh is impossible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the opinions of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding purification when full nazh is impossible, and state the mufta bihi ruling with its justification.

Core Idea
When a flowing well cannot be fully drained, Abu Yusuf's method of estimating the original water volume by expert witnesses is preferred over Muhammad's fixed bucket count.

This lesson addresses a practical difficulty: what if the well is flowing (bi'r mu'ayyanah) and it is physically impossible to draw all the water? The Hanafi school offers two solutions within itself—one by Imam Muhammad (200-300 buckets) and one by Abu Yusuf (estimation by experts). We will examine both, then see why the latter is deemed 'more in line with fiqh' and why it serves as the operative view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception scenario
The well must be 'mu'ayyanah'—a flowing well where drawing all water is impossible (e.g., fed by a spring).
For standing wells, full nazh is possible; this exception applies only to flowing wells.
2
State the two Hanafi opinions
Imam Muhammad: draw 200 to 300 buckets (a fixed approximation). Abu Yusuf: estimate the original volume of water and draw that amount, determined by two qualified experts.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf within the Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
The text says Abu Yusuf's view is 'ashbah bi al-fiqh' (more in line with fiqh) because it considers the actual water volume rather than a fixed number. The mufta bihi is therefore Abu Yusuf's estimation method.
The tarjih authority is the commentator himself (likely Fath al-Qadir or similar).
4
Note the practical procedure
Two trustworthy experts with knowledge of water amounts assess the original volume. The well is then drained by that amount. If that is still impossible, then the ruling of ultimate necessity (istihsan) may apply.
This is a rare case where individual ijtihad of experts is incorporated into a fiqh ruling.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If full nazh is impossible (e.g., a flowing well), Muhammad prescribes 200-300 buckets, while Abu Yusuf says to estimate the original water volume by expert witnesses. For unknown time of fall, Abu Hanifa retroactively applies impurity to three days if swollen/decomposed (since swelling takes 3 days), and one day if not. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say no retroactive impurity unless time is known. Abu Yusuf originally agreed with Abu Hanifa but later recanted when he saw a kite dropping a carcass into a well. The mufta bihi is the opinion of the two: the well is impure from the time the carcass is found, not retroactively.

Key Terms
بئر معينة (bi'r mu'ayyanah): A flowing well (e.g., spring-fed) where drawing all water is impossible.
بصارة (basara): Insight, expertise. Refers to the skill of estimating water volumes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon opinion in the Hanafi school, what should be done when a flowing well (bi'r mu'ayyanah) cannot be fully drained after a swollen animal is found?
A) No purification is needed because the well is flowing.
B) Draw exactly 200 buckets.
C) Have two experts estimate the original water volume and draw that amount.
D) Draw 300 buckets to be safe.

Key Takeaway
When full nazh is impossible in a flowing well, the mufta bihi opinion is to estimate the original water volume through expert witnesses and draw that amount, not a fixed number.

Retroactive Impurity for Unknown Time of Fall
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on retroactive impurity with Abu Yusuf retraction story

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on retroactive impurity when a dead animal is found in a well, and state the mufta bihi ruling with its basis in Abu Yusuf's retraction.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi is that a well becomes impure from the time the carcass is found, not retroactively, unless the time of fall is known.

What if you find a dead mouse in your well but have no idea when it fell in? Have your prayers been valid for the past several days? This lesson tackles the problem of retroactive impurity (tathir madi). Imam Abu Hanifa estimated the time based on swelling (three days if swollen, one day if not). The two, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, said no retroactive estimation—only from the time of discovery. The fascinating story of Abu Yusuf changing his mind after witnessing a kite dropping a carcass into a well illustrates how empirical evidence can shift ijtihad within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A dead animal (e.g., mouse) is found in a well, but the time it fell is unknown. The animal may be swollen/decomposed or not.
The dispute concerns impurity retroactively applied to past days.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
If swollen/decomposed: well is impure from three days ago; prayers of those three days must be repeated. If not swollen: from one day ago.
The estimation is based on how long it takes for a carcass to show these signs (3 days for swelling).
3
State the position of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)
The well becomes impure only from the moment the carcass is found. No prayers need to be repeated unless the exact time of fall is known.
They apply the principle that impurity is established at the time of discovery (yaqeen), not by estimation.
4
Note Abu Yusuf's retraction
Abu Yusuf originally agreed with Abu Hanifa until he witnessed a kite dropping a carcass into a well. This real event showed that an animal could fall in without swelling for three days if it was already dead? Actually, the story indicates that the carcass could be dropped directly into the well, so the swelling time estimation is unreliable. He then retracted and joined Muhammad's view.
This is a famous example of a scholar changing his ijtihad based on observation.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The fatwa is given on the opinion of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the well is impure from the time it is found, unless the time of fall is known.
Thus, no retroactive impurity is established, and past prayers are valid.

(Fath al-Mu'in): Swelling of an animal etc.: All water is drawn if an animal swells or decomposes in it, whether the animal is small or large. Mud does not have to be removed due to hardship, but all water must be removed because moisture spreads through the water; this swelling and disintegration release moisture, and that moisture is liquid impurity like drops of wine or urine. This is in al-Mustakhlas. The difference between swelling (intifakh) and disintegration (takhsukh) is that swelling is inflation of the body where if you wipe its skin with a finger or wood gently, its hair or feathers fall off. Disintegration is that the parts of the dead body become loose and separate entirely or partially after death. (Hashiyah): The 200 buckets etc.: When nazh is impossible, if the well is flowing (ma'in), according to Muhammad, 200 to 300 buckets are drawn; according to Abu Yusuf, the amount of water originally in the well is removed, and this is determined by the opinion of two experts in water matters. This is more in line with fiqh. (Miskin summarized): 'And its becoming impure' etc. is the past tense of tanjis, meaning if a mouse or similar is found in the well and it is not known when it fell, and it is swollen or decomposed, the well becomes impure from three days and nights ago; meaning they repeat the prayers of these days. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two say: they do not have to repeat anything until they ascertain when it fell. (Miskin and others): 'The time of its fall' in the nominative as the subject of 'unknown'; then the estimation is of three days according to the Imam, because the falling of a blood-containing animal into water leads to its death, especially in a well, and the time of falling precedes the time of discovery, so it is estimated at three days because it does not swell except after three days. Abu Yusuf used to follow Abu Hanifa until he saw a kite with a carcass in its beak, which it dropped into a well, so he retracted his opinion. The fatwa is given on their (the two's) opinion: that it becomes impure from the time it is found unless its time is known. (Fath): 'And otherwise' meaning if it is not swollen or decomposed, it becomes impure from one day and night according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to the two.

Commentary
This passage continues the well rulings, focusing on cases where the animal has swollen or decomposed. The matn states that all water must be drawn if the animal shows these signs, regardless of its original size. The commentary explains that swelling (intifakh) and disintegration (takhsukh) release liquid impurity throughout the water. A distinction is made: in swelling, the skin loses hair/feathers easily; in disintegration, parts separate. If full nazh is impossible (e.g., a flowing well), Muhammad prescribes 200-300 buckets, while Abu Yusuf says to estimate the original water volume by expert witnesses. For unknown time of fall, Abu Hanifa retroactively applies impurity to three days if swollen/decomposed (since swelling takes 3 days), and one day if not. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say no retroactive impurity unless time is known. Abu Yusuf originally agreed with Abu Hanifa but later recanted when he saw a kite dropping a carcass into a well. The mufta bihi is the opinion of the two: the well is impure from the time the carcass is found, not retroactively.

Key Terms
تنجيس ماضٍ (tathir madi): Retroactive impurity: declaring that water was impure in the past due to a now-discovered contaminant.
حداءة (huda'ah): A kite (bird of prey). In the story, a kite dropped a carcass into a well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The well is impure only if the rabbit was dead before falling.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi opinion in the Hanafi school regarding unknown fall time is that the well becomes impure only from the moment of discovery, with no retroactive effect, as supported by Abu Yusuf's retraction based on empirical observation.

Rulings on Leftover Water (Su'r) and Sweat (Araq)
Rulings on leftover water and sweat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of humans, animals, and beasts of prey, and apply the principle that sweat follows the ruling of su'r, with the exception of the donkey.

Core Idea
The su'r of a human is pure; the su'r of a dog is impure; and the sweat of a donkey is pure despite its doubtful su'r.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi classification of leftover water (su'r) and sweat (araq) based on the source of the liquid. The matn categorizes su'r into pure (tahir), impure (najis), and doubtful (mashkuk). It also establishes that araq follows the same ruling as su'r, with a special exemption for the donkey. Understanding these categories is essential for determining the purity of water used in wudu and other acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of su'r in the Hanafi school
From the passage, list the beings whose su'r is tahir, najis, or mashkuk. Note that the su'r of a human, horse, and halal meat animals is tahir; dog, swine, and beasts of prey are najis; donkey su'r is doubtful (mashkuk) but its sweat is tahir.
The exception for donkey sweat is based on a specific reason.
2
Understand the general rule that araq follows su'r
The passage states 'al-araq ka al-su'r' meaning the ruling of sweat corresponds to the ruling of leftover water. So if su'r is pure, sweat is pure; if su'r is impure, sweat is impure.
This is a general principle with an exception for the donkey.
3
Recognize the cross-madhhab differences
The commentary notes that Imam Malik holds that dog and pig su'r are not impure, and Imam al-Shafi'i holds that beasts of prey su'r are not impure. Contrast with the Hanafi position.
These differences affect the practical rulings for purification.

Rulings of the leftover water: and sweat is like leftover water. The leftover water of a human, horse, and what is eaten of its meat is pure. The dog and swine: the leftover water of the dog = the leftover water of the horse. (The text then repeats previous commentary on swelling, which seems out of place. It continues): And sweat is like leftover water: meaning the sweat of everything is considered according to its leftover water in terms of purity, impurity, prohibition, and dislike. It is not contradicted by the sweat of a donkey because its sweat is pure, not doubtful, even though by analogy its leftover water is doubtful; this is because (the donkey) is singled out for riding with bare back and exposed, and (it carries) the heavy burdens of Hijaz and the weight of prophethood, so the ruling on others remains by analogy. (Fath, Miskin): The leftover water of a human etc.: meaning absolutely, whether pure, junub, hadath, menstruating, postpartum, small, large, Muslim, disbeliever, male, female, except when drinking wine; if he swallows his saliva three times, his mouth becomes pure. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 23/1). And the horse is mentioned specifically due to the difference of opinion about its meat; because its meat is haram according to Abu Hanifa, yet its leftover water is pure because the prohibition of its meat is for honor, not impurity. Do you not see that its milk is halal by consensus? And His statement: 'pure' is the predicate of the subject, meaning his statement: 'and the leftover water of a human.' (Mustakhlas, Ayni): And the dog etc. in the nominative by deletion of the added word and substituting the addendum in its place, i.e., the leftover water of the dog and beasts of prey like the lion, tiger, wolf, and similar is impure, contrary to Malik regarding the dog and pig, and contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding beasts of prey. And it is not permissible to touch it... (the text cuts off).
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the purity of leftover water (su'r) and sweat (araq) of various beings. The matn states that su'r of a human, horse, and animals whose meat is eaten is pure (tahir). The su'r of dogs, swine, and predatory animals (lion, tiger, wolf) is impure (najis). Sweat follows the same ruling as su'r: pure for pure su'r, impure for impure su'r. An exception is the donkey: its su'r is considered doubtful (mashkuk), but its sweat is pure (tahir) due to special exemption (it was ridden) contrary to the analogy. The commentary explains that human su'r is pure regardless of the person's state (janabah, menstruation, etc.) except when the mouth is contaminated with wine (then one must swallow saliva three times to purify). Horse su'r is pure even though its meat is haram according to Abu Hanifa, because the prohibition is for honor not impurity. The dog and swine su'r is impure, and this is a point of difference with Imam Malik (who considers dog and pig su'r not impure) and Imam al-Shafi'i (who considers su'r of beasts of prey not impure). The text cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
السؤر (al-su'r): The water left over in a vessel after an animal or human drinks from it.
العرق (al-araq): Sweat or perspiration of a living being.
سباع البهائم (siba' al-baha'im): Predatory animals from among beasts, such as lions, tigers, wolves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Doubtful (mashkuk)
D) Permissible but disliked (makruh)

Key Takeaway
The ruling on leftover water and sweat in the Hanafi school depends on the source: humans, horses, and halal meat animals produce pure su'r; dogs, swine, and beasts of prey produce impure su'r; the donkey's sweat is pure despite its doubtful su'r.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Well Water Impurity: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Ruling on well water contamination and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of well water impurity when a dead mouse is found and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When a dead mouse is found in a well, Abu Hanifa estimates impurity retroactively; the Sahibayn limit it to the time of discovery.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the impurity of well water when a dead mouse (or similar animal) is discovered. The core issue is not whether the water becomes impure—that is agreed—but from what moment it becomes impure and whether past prayers must be repeated. The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, reflects different methodologies in dealing with uncertainty. By understanding their proofs and the eventual tarjih, you will appreciate how the Hanafi school refines its positions over time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed ruling
Both parties agree that a dead mouse in well water makes the water najis (impure). Confirm the consequence: the water cannot be used for purification until the well is purified (drained).
2
State Abu Hanifa’s position and his rational proof
Abu Hanifa holds that if the mouse is swollen or disintegrated, the impurity is retroactive to three days prior; if not swollen, to one day prior. His proof: swelling only occurs after three days, so the time of death can be estimated.
This is a dalil aqli (rational evidence) based on empirical observation.
3
State the Sahibayn’s position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that impurity starts only from the time of discovery unless the exact time of the fall is known. Their proof: retroactive estimation is speculative, and certainty is required before declaring impurity.
They prefer caution in declaring previous acts invalid.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf’s retraction and the tarjih
Abu Yusuf initially agreed with Abu Hanifa but later retracted after witnessing a kite drop a carcass into a well, realizing the difficulty of precise timing. The mufta bihi (operative fatwa) is now the view of the Sahibayn.
This illustrates how practical experience can influence ijtihad.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa's view, one must repeat all prayers performed during the estimated period; under the Sahibayn's view, no repetition is required unless the exact time is known.
The mufta bihi spares the believer from unnecessary qada.

منها بلة، وتلك البلة نجاسة مائعة بمنزلة القطر من الخمر أو البول، كذا في "المستخلص". والفرق بين الانتفاخ والتفسخ أن الانتفاخ تورم في جسد الميت بحيث لو مسح جلده بإصبع أو حطب بالرفق لزال شعره وريشه، والتفسخ : أن يتمعط أجزاء الميت ويتفرق كلها أو بعضها بعد الموت. (محشي) ومائتان إلخ: عدم إمكان النزح إذا كانت البئر معينة أي جارية، فعند محمد ينزح مائتا دلو إلى ثلاث مائة، وعند أبي يوسف يخرج مقدار ما كان فيها من الماء، وطريق معرفته أن يؤخذ بقول رجلين لهما بصارة في أمور الماء، وهذا أشبه بالفقه مسكين ملخصاً) ونجسها إلخ ماض من التنجيس، يعني إذا وجد في البئر فارة أو نحوها و لم يدر متى وقعت وقد انتفخت أو تفسخت ينجس البئر مذ ثلاثة أيام ولياليها، يعني أعادوا صلاة هذه الأيام، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : ليس عليهم إعادة شيء حتى يحققوا متى وقعت. (مسكين وغيره) وقت وقوعها بالرفع فاعل "جهل"، ثم التقدير بثلاث مذهب الإمام؛ لأن وقوع الحيوان الدموي في الماء لموته لاسيما في البئر ، وزمان الوقوع سابق على زمان الوجود، فقدر بثلاثة أيام؛ لأنه لا ينتفخ إلا بعد ثلاثة أيام، وأبو يوسف كان يقول بقول أبي حنيفة إلى أن رأى حداءة في منقارها جيفة، فطرحتها في بئر فرجع عن قوله، والمفتى به قولهما، أي يتنجس مذ وجد إلا أن يعلم وقتها. (فتح)
سبب
وإلا مذ يوم أي وإن لم تكن منتفخة أو متفسخة نجسها مذ يوم وليلة عنده، خلافاً لهما. (ط)
Book of Purification, page 29. Rulings of Wells. And two hundred [buckets] if its drainage is not possible, and its impurity [is] from three [days] for a mouse swollen or disintegrated, the time of its fall unknown, otherwise from a day and a night. Rulings of Wells: i.e., the well. ... from it moisture, and that moisture is liquid impurity like drops of wine or urine, as in al-Mustakhlas. The difference between swelling and disintegration is that swelling is a swelling in the body of the dead such that if one wipes its skin with a finger or a stick gently, its hair or feathers fall off; disintegration is that the parts of the dead become separated and all or some scatter after death. (Mahshi) 'And two hundred etc.': The impossibility of draining if the well is a flowing well. According to Muhammad, two hundred buckets up to three hundred are drained; according to Abu Yusuf, the amount of water that was in it is removed, and the way to know it is that the statement of two men who have insight in water matters is taken, and this is more akin to fiqh (Miskin summarised). 'And its impurity etc.' is from tanjis, meaning if a mouse or the like is found in a well and it is not known when it fell, and it is swollen or disintegrated, the well is impure from three days and their nights, meaning they repeat the prayers of these days. This is according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: they do not have to repeat anything until they ascertain when it fell. (Miskin and others) 'The time of its fall' is in the nominative as the subject of 'unknown'. Then the estimation is three [days] according to the Imam's school; because the fall of a blooded animal into water due to its death, especially in a well, and the time of the fall precedes the time of finding, so it is estimated as three days because it does not swell except after three days. Abu Yusuf used to say with Abu Hanifa's statement until he saw a kite with a carcass in its beak which it threw into a well, so he retracted his statement. The mufta bihi is their statement (the two), i.e., it becomes impure from the time it is found unless its time is known. (Fath) 'Cause' and 'Otherwise from a day' means if it is not swollen or disintegrated, its impurity is from a day and a night according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to them (the two). (T)
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage concerns the ruling of well water when a dead mouse (or similar animal) is found. The matn states the basic ruling: if the mouse is swollen or disintegrated and the time of its fall is unknown, the water is considered impure for three days and nights; otherwise, for one day and night. The commentary explains that 'two hundred' refers to buckets of water drained if the well is not flowing. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the water is impure from three days prior, requiring repetition of prayers during that period, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that no repetition is required until the exact time is known. Abu Yusuf later retracted his original agreement with Abu Hanifa after seeing a kite drop a carcass into a well, and the mufta bihi (operative fatwa) is the view of the two, i.e., impurity starts from the time of discovery unless the time is known. The text also distinguishes between 'swelling' (intifakh) where hair falls off easily and 'disintegration' (tafaskh) where parts separate. The estimation of three days is based on the fact that swelling only occurs after three days, making it a rational estimation (dalil aqli). The commentary also notes that if the mouse is not swollen or disintegrated, Abu Hanifa holds impurity from one day and night, while the Sahibayn differ.

Key Terms
نزح (nazḥ): Draining or bailing out water from a well.
منتفخة (muntafikhah): Swollen, referring to a dead animal whose body has inflated due to decomposition.
متفسخة (mutafaskhah): Disintegrated, where the body parts separate or decay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative) view in the Hanafi school, if a swollen mouse is found in a well and the time of its fall is unknown, from when is the water considered impure?
A) From three days prior to discovery.
B) From one day prior to discovery.
C) From the time of discovery.
D) The water is not impure at all.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school for an unknown-time dead mouse in a well is that the water is impure only from the time of discovery, not retroactively.

Sweat of an Animal Follows Its Su'ur
Ruling that sweat follows su'ur with an exception for the donkey

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that sweat takes the ruling of su'ur (leftover water) and explain the Hanafi exception for the donkey with its legal basis.

Core Idea
Sweat takes the ruling of su'ur, except the donkey's sweat is pure due to Prophetic practice.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes a key principle in Hanafi taharah: the sweat of an animal inherits the same legal classification as its su'ur (leftover water). However, there is a notable exception for the donkey, whose sweat is ruled pure despite its su'ur being doubtful. Understanding this rule helps you determine the purity of animal sweat in various contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage states that the sweat of everything is considered according to its su'ur in terms of purity, impurity, prohibition, and dislike. This means the ruling of sweat is derived from the ruling of the leftover water of that animal.
2
Recognize the exception
The donkey is an exception: its sweat is pure even though its su'ur is considered mashkuk (doubtful). So the general analogy (qiyas) would have made the sweat doubtful, but a specific evidence overrides it.
3
Understand the rationale
The exception is based on the fact that the Prophet (ﷺ) rode a donkey bare-backed (without a saddle) and the sweat would have contacted him. Since the Prophet's practice indicates no concern, the sweat is ruled pure. This special honor (tashrif) removes the doubt.
The phrase 'حر حر الحجاز' and 'ثقل ثقل النبوة' poetically reinforce the idea that the donkey carried the Prophet and the weight of revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعرق كالسؤر: يعني عرق كل شيء يعتبر بسؤره طهارة ونجاسة وحرمة وكراهة، ولا ينتقض بعرق الحمار؛ لأن عرقه طاهر لا مشكوك وإن كان قياس كون سؤره مشكوكاً أن يكون عرقه كذلك؛ لأنه خص بركوبه عري الظهر ومكشوفه، والحر حر الحجاز والثقل ثقل النبوة، فبقي الحكم في غيره على القياس. (فتح، مسكين)
And sweat is like leftover water: meaning the sweat of everything is considered according to its leftover water in purity, impurity, prohibition, and dislike. And it is not contradicted by the sweat of the donkey, because its sweat is pure, not doubtful, although by analogy its leftover water being doubtful would make its sweat likewise; but it is distinguished by its riding (the Prophet ﷺ rode it) bare-backed and uncovered, and 'the free' is the free of Hijaz and 'the burden' is the burden of prophethood, so the ruling remains for other than it upon analogy. (Fath, Miskin)
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This short passage establishes the rule that the sweat ('araq) of an animal takes the same legal classification as its su'ur (leftover water). Thus, if an animal's su'ur is pure, its sweat is pure; if impure, its sweat is impure; if makruh, its sweat is makruh. An exception is noted regarding the donkey: although its su'ur is considered mashkuk (doubtful), its sweat is ruled pure. This exception is based on a specific evidence: the Prophet (ﷺ) rode a donkey while it was bare-backed, and the sweat would have come into contact with him, indicating its purity. The reasoning is that the donkey was specially favored by being ridden by the Prophet, so its sweat is exempt from the general analogy. For all other animals, the general rule applies: sweat follows the ruling of su'ur.

Key Terms
العرق (al-'araq): Sweat or perspiration of an animal.
السؤر (al-su'ur): The water left over after an animal drinks, or the moisture from its mouth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of the sweat of a donkey according to the Hanafi school?
A) Impure, because its su'ur is mashkuk.
B) Pure, because the Prophet rode it bare-backed.
C) Makruh, like its su'ur.
D) It is mashkuk, like its su'ur.

Key Takeaway
Sweat inherits the ruling of leftover water; only the donkey's sweat is an exception due to Prophetic practice.

The Purity of Su'ur: Humans, Horses, and Predators
Ruling on su'ur of humans, horses, and edible animals; impurity of predators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the su'ur (leftover water) of various creatures and explain the reasoning behind the purity of human and horse su'ur.

Core Idea
Su'ur follows the flesh: pure flesh means pure su'ur; impure flesh means impure su'ur.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes the Hanafi position on the purity of residual water (su'ur) left by humans, horses, and edible animals. It also clarifies the exceptional case of a person drinking wine and addresses the impurity of dogs and beasts of prey. The reasoning hinges on the status of the animal's flesh – whether it is pure or impure. The text also notes differences with the Maliki and Shafi'i schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the human su'ur ruling
The passage states that human su'ur is pure unconditionally, regardless of the person's state (junub, menstruating, etc.), with one exception: when the person is drinking wine, the mouth must be purified by swallowing saliva three times.
The exception is due to the impurity of wine, not the person.
2
Analyze the horse su'ur case
Horse su'ur is pure even though Abu Hanifa considers horse meat haram. The prohibition of horse meat is for honor (karama), not impurity, as evidenced by the consensus that horse milk is halal.
The ruling is based on the principle that the animal's flesh must be impure for the su'ur to be impure.
3
Generalize to edible animals
By implication, the su'ur of any animal whose meat is halal to eat is pure. This includes cows, sheep, chickens, etc.
Edible animals are defined by their meat being permissible.
4
Identify impure su'ur categories
The su'ur of dogs and beasts of prey (lions, tigers, wolves) is impure. This is proven by the hadith about purifying a vessel from a dog's lick, and by analogy to other predators.
Beasts of prey are those that hunt with fangs.
5
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam Malik differs regarding dogs and pigs; Imam al-Shafi'i differs regarding beasts of prey. The Hanafi school adheres to the position of impurity based on the hadith and reasoning.
Practical consequence: Hanafis consider water drunk by a dog impure; Malikis may allow its use under certain conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسؤر الآدمي إلخ: أي مطلقاً سواء كان طاهراً أو جنباً أو محدثاً أو حائضاً أو نفساء أو صغيرًا أو كبيراً أو مسلماً أو كافراً أو ذكراً أو أنثى، لا حالة شربه الخمر، فإن بلع ريقه ثلاث مرات طهر فمه (رمز الحقائق: ٢٣/١) وأفرد الفرس بالذكر لمكان الاختلاف في لحمه؛ لأن لحمه حرام عند أبي حنيفة، ومع ذلك سؤره طاهر؛ لأن حرمة لحمه لكرامة لا لنجاسة، ألا ترى أن لبنه حلال بالإجماع، وقوله : "طاهر" خبر المبتدأ يعني قوله: وسؤر الآدمي. (مستخلص، عيني) والكلب إلخ بالرفع على حذف المضاف وإقامة المضاف إليه مقامه أي وسؤر الكلب وسباع البهائم كالأسد والنمر والذئب ونحوها نجس خلافاً لمالك في الكلب والخنزير وللشافعي في سباع البهائم. ولا يجوز جره =
And the su'ur of humans etc.: i.e., absolutely, whether the person is pure, junub, hadath, menstruating, postnatal, young, old, Muslim, kafir, male, or female, except when drinking wine, for if he swallows his saliva three times his mouth becomes pure (Ramz al-Haqa'iq). And the horse is mentioned specifically because of the difference of opinion about its meat; for its meat is haram according to Abu Hanifa, yet its su'ur is pure because the prohibition of its meat is for honor ('karama') not impurity. Do you not see that its milk is halal by consensus? And his statement 'pure' is the predicate of the subject, meaning his statement: and the su'ur of humans. (Mustakhlas, 'Ayni) And the dog etc. is in the nominative with the deletion of the noun and the standing of the genitive in its place, i.e., the su'ur of the dog and beasts of prey like lion, tiger, wolf, etc. are impure, contrary to Malik regarding the dog and pig, and contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding beasts of prey. And it is not permitted to drag?
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of su'ur (leftover water) from various creatures. First, it establishes that the su'ur of a human is always pure, regardless of the person's state of ritual purity (even if junub, menstruating, etc.), except if the person is drinking wine; then the mouth must be cleaned by swallowing saliva three times. The horse is mentioned because there is a difference of opinion about eating its meat: Abu Hanifa considers horse meat haram (disliked), yet its su'ur is pure because the prohibition is due to honor not impurity, analogous to its milk being halal by consensus. For animals whose meat is edible (such as cows, sheep, etc.), their su'ur is pure by extension. Then the text moves to impure su'ur: the su'ur of dogs and beasts of prey (like lions, tigers, wolves) is impure. This is contrary to Imam Malik who holds dog and pig su'ur as less impure? And contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i regarding beasts of prey. The proof for impurity is likely from hadith (e.g., the dog's saliva).

Key Terms
السؤر (al-su'ur): The leftover water in a vessel after an animal drinks from it, or the moisture from the animal's mouth.
سباع البهائم (sibā‘ al-bahā’im): Beasts of prey among land animals, such as lions, tigers, wolves, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of the su'ur of a lion?
A) Pure
B) Impure
C) Makruh
D) Mashkuk

Key Takeaway
The purity of su'ur is directly tied to the status of the animal's flesh: pure flesh yields pure su'ur; impure flesh yields impure su'ur.

Su'ur of Cats, Free-Roaming Animals: Makruh Tanzihan
Ruling that su'ur of certain animals is makruh tanzihan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'ur of a domestic cat, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and apply the principle of combining conflicting evidences to derive the ruling of karahah.

Core Idea
Cat su'ur is makruh tanzihan, not pure and not impure, as a compromise between conflicting hadith.

The su'ur (leftover water) of a domestic cat is a classic example of how Hanafi jurists reconcile apparently conflicting textual proofs. This lesson examines the evidences, the differing opinion of Abu Yusuf, and the reason the school settled on karahah tanzihiyah. Understanding this ruling helps you appreciate the method of jam' (reconciliation) and the importance of noting the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its ruling
Identify what is being ruled: the su'ur (leftover water) of a domestic cat, a free-roaming chicken, and birds of prey. The ruling given is makruh tanzihan (disliked but not prohibited) when other water is available.
The ruling applies only when other water exists; if no other water, using it is permissible.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Find the main proof cited: The hadith 'The cat is a beast of prey' (al-sinnawru sab'un) reported by al-Hakim. This suggests impurity because beasts of prey have impure su'ur according to some.
The hadith is used to establish the potential impurity, but it is not taken as absolute.
3
Identify the opposing evidence and view
Note that Abu Yusuf holds cat su'ur is pure (tahir) with no dislike, based on a hadith about a cat drinking from a vessel (hadith al-isgha'). Some versions mention that the Prophet allowed using water after a cat drunk.
Abu Yusuf's view is that the su'ur is absolutely pure.
4
Understand the reconciliation
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) combine the two proofs: the hadith indicating impurity is weakened because it was revealed in the context of tawaf or is not general, so they do not declare impurity but rather karahah. This is a compromise (jam' bayn al-dalilayn).
The ruling of karahah tanzihiyah respects both proofs without fully adopting either.
5
Apply the ruling to other animals
The same ruling applies to free-roaming chickens (mukhallah) and birds of prey. A free-roaming chicken that eats filth (jallalah) also has makruh su'ur, whereas a confined chicken does not. Similarly, house-dwelling animals (sawakina al-buyut) follow the same pattern.
The key factor is the animal's lifestyle: roaming and potentially eating impure substances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والهرة إلخ: أي سؤر الهرة الأهلية مكروه كراهة تنزيهية؛ لقوله علية: "السنور سبع" أخرجه الحاكم، والمراد بيان الحكم، وقال أبو يوسف: سؤرها طاهر لا كراهة فيه؛ لحديث الإصغاء، وبه قالت الثلاثة، ولهما: أن الحديث يقتضي تنجسه، ولكنه سقط لعلة الطواف، والقول بالكراهة جمع بين الدليلين. (رمز الحقائق: ٢٣/١) المخلاة: أي المسيبة، وكذا شاة جلالة، بخلاف محبوسة فلا يكره سؤرها. (ط) مكروه تنزيهاً عند وجود غيره. (ط)
And the cat etc.: i.e., the su'ur of the domestic cat is makruh tanzihan (disliked but not prohibited), because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'The cat is a beast of prey' reported by al-Hakim, and the intent is to clarify the ruling. Abu Yusuf said: its su'ur is pure, no dislike in it, due to the hadith of 'listening'? and the three (Imams) said likewise. And for them (the two, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?): the hadith necessitates its impurity, but it dropped due to the cause of tawaf, and the ruling of karahah is a combination of the two evidences. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq) 'Al-mukhallah': i.e., the one left free, and likewise a jallalah sheep, unlike one confined, so its su'ur is not makruh. (T) Makruh tanzihan when other water is available. (T)
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage deals with the su'ur of the domestic cat, free-roaming chickens (mukhallah), birds of prey, and house-dwelling animals. The ruling is that their su'ur is makruh tanzihan (disliked but not impure). The primary evidence is a hadith: 'The cat is a beast of prey' (reported by al-Hakim), which suggests impurity. However, there is also a hadith about a cat drinking from a vessel that indicates permissibility. Abu Yusuf holds that cat su'ur is absolutely pure with no dislike, based on the hadith of 'listening' (possibly referring to the hadith of the cat that was allowed to drink from the Prophet's vessel). The majority of the three (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and others?) hold the makruh view as a compromise: the hadith implying impurity is weakened because it was abrogated or not applicable due to the context of tawaf, so the ruling of karahah balances the evidences. The text also specifies that the ruling applies to free-roaming cats, not confined ones. For chickens, only those that roam freely (mukhallah) are makruh; tied chickens are not. Similarly, a jallalah (animal fed on filth) has makruh su'ur, but if confined and fed clean food, it is not makruh. Birds of prey are included by analogy. The ruling is only when other water is available; if none, it is permissible.

Key Terms
المخلاة (al-mukhallāh): An animal left free to roam and eat what it finds, such as a free-roaming chicken.
الجلالة (al-jallālah): An animal that eats filth or impure substances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of the su'ur of a domestic cat?
A) Pure and allowed without dislike.
B) Impure and cannot be used.
C) Makruh tanzihan when other water is available.
D) Mashkuk (doubtful).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on cat su'ur is makruh tanzihan, reconciled from conflicting hadith, with the dislike dropping when no alternative water exists.
