Conditions and Nullifiers of Tayammum
States the conditions for valid tayammum, its ruling for a disbeliever, and what nullifies it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid tayammum, identify the rulings for a disbeliever's tayammum and wudu, explain why apostasy does not nullify tayammum, and apply the rule that tayammum is nullified by what nullifies wudu, including its exception.

Core Idea
Tayammum is a valid substitute for wudu/ghusl, requiring intention, and its nullifiers mirror those of wudu with a critical nuance.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays down the foundational rules for tayammum. It addresses the necessity of intention, the special case of a disbeliever's purification, and the effect of apostasy. Most importantly, it establishes that tayammum is nullified by whatever nullifies wudu, with a nuanced exception that distinguishes between tayammum for minor and major impurity.

Guided Path
1
Classify the act: tayammum as a substitute purification
Recognize that tayammum is a badal (substitute) for wudu or ghusl when water is absent or unusable. This substitution carries implications for its conditions and nullifiers.
The substitute takes the ruling of the original except where specified otherwise.
2
Identify the condition of intention and the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that the matn states tayammum is valid with intention (niyyah). The majority of Hanafis require intention; Imam Zufar disagrees, considering tayammum a purely physical act. Determine the mufta bihi: intention is required.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if one performs tayammum absentmindedly, it is invalid according to the majority but valid according to Zufar.
3
Determine the ruling for a disbeliever's tayammum and wudu
The matn says a disbeliever's tayammum is invalid, but his wudu is not. Analyze: tayammum by a disbeliever is only valid if done for the purpose of entering Islam (niyyah of Islam), not for prayer. For wudu, if a disbeliever performs wudu intending to become Muslim, it becomes valid upon conversion, contrary to al-Shafi'i who requires intention as a condition.
The dispute with Shafi'i hinges on whether niyyah is a condition for wudu; Hanafis do not require niyyah for wudu, so a disbeliever's wudu is valid.
4
Assess the effect of apostasy on tayammum
The matn states apostasy does not nullify a previously valid tayammum. If a Muslim performs tayammum, then apostatizes and later returns to Islam, the tayammum remains valid. This is contrary to Zufar who held that apostasy nullifies it.
Apostasy does not nullify any ritual purification in the Hanafi school; it only affects the validity of worship if one apostatizes in between.
5
Apply the nullification rule and its exception
The matn says tayammum is nullified by what nullifies wudu. However, the commentator (Fath) notes an exception: if one performs tayammum for janabah (major impurity) and then experiences minor hadath, only the part of tayammum that substitutes for wudu is nullified, not the tayammum for ghusl. Thus, not everything that nullifies wudu nullifies all tayammum.
This nuance arises because tayammum can serve as a substitute for both wudu and ghusl, each with its own nullification rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح التيمم بلا عجز ناوياً، فلغا تيمم كافر لا وضوؤه، ولا ينقضه ردّة بل ناقض الوضوء. (ط) ناوياً : أي يتيمم ناوياً استباحة الصلاة أو قربة لا تتأدى بلا طهارة، وعند زفر نيته ليست بشرط (ط) تيمم كافر للإسلام، وأما إذا تيمم للصلاة فلا يجوز بالاتفاق؛ لأن الكافر ليس من أهلها، وفي الوضوء خلاف الشافعي؛ لافتقاره إلى النية عنده، والكافر ليس من أهلها. (فتح) ولا ينقضه: أي إن توضأ الكافر للإسلام ثم أسلم فهو متوضئ خلافاً للشافعي ردّة: فلو تيمم مسلم ثم ارتد - والعياذ بالله - ثم أسلم فهو على تيممه خلافاً لزفر. (ط) بل ناقض الوضوء أي ينقضه ما ينقض الوضوء؛ لأنه خلفه، فيأخذ حكمه، ولو قال: ناقض الأصل ليعم الوضوء والغسل لكان أحسن؛ لأنه ليس كل ما ينقض الوضوء ينقض التيمم كما إذا تيمم لجنابة ثم عرضه الحدث الأصغر انتقض تيمم الوضوء دون تيمم الغسل. (فتح)
And tayammum is valid without inability with intention. So the tayammum of a disbeliever is invalid, not his wudu. Apostasy does not nullify it, but what nullifies wudu does. (T) 'with intention': meaning he performs tayammum intending to permit prayer or an act of worship that cannot be performed without purification. According to Zufar, intention is not a condition. (T) 'tayammum of a disbeliever' for Islam. As for if he performs tayammum for prayer, it is not valid by agreement, because the disbeliever is not among its people. Regarding wudu, there is disagreement with al-Shafi'i because it requires intention according to him, and the disbeliever is not among its people. (Fath) 'Apostasy does not nullify it': that is, if a disbeliever performs wudu for Islam then becomes Muslim, he is in a state of wudu, contrary to al-Shafi'i. If as a Muslim he performs tayammum then apostatizes (Allah forbid) then returns to Islam, he remains on his tayammum, contrary to Zufar. (T) 'but what nullifies wudu does' meaning it is nullified by what nullifies wudu, because it is a substitute for wudu, so it takes its ruling. If he said 'nullifier of the original' to include wudu and ghusl it would be better, because not everything that nullifies wudu nullifies tayammum, as when he performs tayammum for janabah then minor hadath occurs, his tayammum for wudu is nullified but not his tayammum for ghusl. (Fath)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq sets forth several rules regarding tayammum. First, for tayammum to be valid, one must have intention (niyyah) to permit prayer or worship that requires purification. The commentator notes that Imam Zufar disagrees and does not require intention. Second, the tayammum of a disbeliever is only valid if done for the purpose of entering Islam; if done for prayer, it is invalid because the disbeliever is not a qualified worshipper. Regarding wudu, the commentator notes that if a disbeliever performs wudu for Islam then becomes Muslim, his wudu is valid, contrary to Shafi'i who requires intention. Third, apostasy does not nullify tayammum; if a Muslim performs tayammum then apostatizes and returns to Islam, his tayammum remains valid—contrary to Zufar. Fourth, tayammum is nullified by whatever nullifies wudu, because tayammum is a substitute. However, the commentator cautions that not everything that nullifies wudu nullifies tayammum: for example, if one performs tayammum for janabah (major impurity) and then experiences minor hadath, only the tayammum for wudu (i.e., the part of tayammum that substitutes for wudu) is nullified, not the tayammum for ghusl.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention to perform tayammum for the sake of worship (e.g., to permit prayer).
ردّة (riddah): Apostasy from Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a Muslim performs tayammum, then apostatizes, then returns to Islam, what is the status of the tayammum?
A) It is nullified by the apostasy.
B) It remains valid, and he can pray without renewing it.
C) It depends on whether he intended to remain Muslim.
D) He must repeat tayammum because he is a new convert.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum requires intention, is valid for a disbeliever only for Islam, is not nullified by apostasy, and is nullified by the same things that nullify wudu, with the exception that tayammum for ghusl is not nullified by minor hadath.

Ability to Obtain Water Nullifies Tayammum
Ruling on ability to obtain water and its effect on tayammum, with proof and inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when ability to obtain water prevents and nullifies tayammum, and explain the evidence from Quran and the difference with Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Ability to obtain water ends tayammum immediately, even during prayer.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with commentary from Fath al-Mu'in, addresses the crucial condition of water availability for tayammum. The Hanafi school interprets 'finding water' in the Quran as 'ability to use it,' leading to rulings that differ from the Shafi'i school. You will examine the proof and the inter-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm
The matn states that ability to obtain water prevents tayammum initially and nullifies it if already performed.
Note: 'prevents' means it is not permissible to perform tayammum; 'nullifies' means an existing tayammum becomes invalid.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator references Quran 4:43: 'then you did not find water' and explains that 'finding' is interpreted as ability.
This interpretation is key to the Hanafi position.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The term 'finding' (وجد) is expanded to mean 'ability' to include cases where water is present but cannot be used due to illness or cold.
Thus, mere sight without ability does not nullify tayammum.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that obtaining water during a prayer performed with tayammum does not nullify the tayammum because the prayer's sanctity prevents it.
The Hanafi response is that actual ability takes precedence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi argument is that the person is truly able, so the condition for tayammum is lost; the prayer's sanctity depends on valid purification.
Thus, the tayammum is invalidated and the prayer must be repeated with wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقدرة ماء فضل عن حاجته فهي تمنع التيمم وترفعه وراجي الماء يؤخر الصلاة، قبل الوقت، ولفرضين وخوف فوت صلاة جنازة أو عيد ولو بناء. (فتح المعين) وقدرة ماء: أشار به إلى أن الوجدان في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً﴾ (النساء: ٤٣) بمعنى القدرة، وعدل عن رؤية الماء إلى القدرة؛ لشمولها ما لو تيمم لبرد أو مرض، وخرج بها ما لو مرَّ النائم بصفة لا توجب النقض على ماء كاف حيث لا ينتقض تيممه. (فتح المعين) تمنع التيمم: يعني إذا كان قدرة الماء ناقض التيمم فتمنع التيمم ابتداءً وتنقضه انتهاءً مطلقاً، سواء كانت قدرته في الصلاة أو في غيرها، وقال الشافعي: لا يرفع التيمم إذا قدر على الماء بعد ما شرع في الصلاة؛ لأن حرمة الصلاة مانعة عن إبطالها، فكان عاجزاً عن الاستعمال حكماً، ولنا أنه قادر حقيقة فيبطل تيممه، ولا يبقى للصلاة حرمة لفوات شرطها؛ لأن التراب لم يجعل طهوراً إلا . عند عدم الماء فيبطل بوجوده. (فتح المعين) يؤخر الصلاة: أي يستحب لعادم الماء إذا غلب على رأيه القدرة عليه أن يؤخر الصلاة حتى يؤديه بأكمل الطهارتين، وظاهر إطلاقه يشمل صلاة المغرب، فيؤخر إلى غيبوبة الشفق وهو الذي عليه الأكثر، وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف في غير رواية الأصول أن التأخير واجب؛ لأن غلبة الرأي كالمتحقق وعن. مالك: المندوب أن في وسط الوقت، وإذا لم يرج الأفضل صلاة في أول الوقت اتفاقاً. (فتح المعين قبل الوقت إلخ: خلافاً للشافعي في تلك المسألتين والخلاف بيننا وبينه يبتني على أن التيمم عندنا طهارة مطلقة يرتفع به الحدث إلى وقت وجود مبيح مع قيام الحدث، وعنده بدل ضروري مبيح مع قيام الحدث حقيقة. (فتح المعين) ولو بناءً [ أي لو كانت صلاته بناء كما لو شرع فيها بالوضوء ثم سبقه حدث تيمم ييني خلافا لهما. (ط)] وقالا : يتيمم ويتوضأ ويتم صلاته، ولا خلاف في أنه إذا شرع بالتيمم يتيمم، وكذا لو شرع بالوضوء ثم أحدث ويخاف زوال الشمس إذا اشتغل بالوضوء تيمم اتفاقاً، فإن لم يخف ويرجو إدراك الإمام قبل الفراغ لم يتيمم إجماعاً. (مسكين)
And the ability to obtain water beyond his need prevents tayammum and nullifies it. And one who hopes for water delays the prayer, before the time, and for two obligatory prayers, and out of fear of missing a funeral prayer or Eid, even if it is a building upon. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Ability to obtain water': he indicated thereby that 'finding' in His statement 'then you did not find water' (4:43) means ability. He turned from seeing water to ability to include cases of tayammum due to cold or illness, and excluded cases where a sleeping person passes by a sufficient [؟] in a way that does not necessitate nullification, so his tayammum is not nullified. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Prevents tayammum': meaning that if ability to obtain water is a nullifier of tayammum, it prevents tayammum initially and nullifies it absolutely, whether his ability occurs during prayer or outside it. Al-Shafi'i said: it does not nullify tayammum if he obtains water after starting prayer, because the sanctity of prayer prevents its invalidation, so he is considered legally unable to use it. Our argument: he is actually able, so his tayammum becomes invalid, and the prayer loses its sanctity due to the loss of its condition, because dust was not made a purifier except in the absence of water, so it is invalidated by its presence. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Delays the prayer': i.e., it is recommended for one who lacks water, if he strongly thinks he can obtain it, to delay the prayer until he performs it with the better of the two purifications. The apparent scope includes the Maghrib prayer, so he delays until the disappearance of the twilight, which is the view of the majority. From Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, in non-riwayah al-usul, that delaying is obligatory, because strong presumption is like actuality. From Malik, it is recommended to pray in the middle of the time. If he does not hope, the best is to pray at the beginning of the time by agreement. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Before the time, etc.': contrary to al-Shafi'i in these two issues. The disagreement between us and him is based on the fact that tayammum in our view is an absolute purification that removes hadath until the time when a permitter is found while hadath remains; according to him, it is a necessary substitute that permits while hadath actually remains. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Even if it is building': that is, if his prayer is a building, as if he began with wudu then an event preceded him, he performs tayammum and builds, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The two said: he performs tayammum and wudu and completes his prayer. There is no disagreement that if he begins with tayammum, he performs tayammum. Similarly, if he begins with wudu then has hadath and fears the sun will set if he occupies himself with wudu, he performs tayammum by agreement. If he does not fear and hopes to catch the imam before finishing, he does not perform tayammum unanimously. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage deals with two related issues: the effect of ability to obtain water on tayammum, and the recommendation to delay prayer when hoping for water. The matn says that ability to obtain surplus water prevents performing tayammum initially and also nullifies an existing tayammum. The commentator explains that the Quranic term 'finding' (فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا) is interpreted as ability (قدرة), not mere sight, to include cases like cold or illness that prevent using water. He records a dispute with Shafi'i: Shafi'i says if one starts prayer with tayammum then obtains water, the prayer is valid and tayammum is not nullified because the prayer's sanctity prevents nullification; Hanafis argue that since one is actually able to use water, the tayammum becomes invalid and the prayer condition is lost. Regarding delaying prayer, the majority holds it is recommended (mustahab) for one who strongly suspects water will appear to delay until near the end of prayer time to perform with water; some narrations from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say it is wajib. The commentator also addresses the case of 'building upon' (ببناء) when one starts with wudu, then has hadath, and has hope of water—there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether he can combine tayammum and wudu. The key underlying principle is that for Hanafis, tayammum is an absolute purification (طهارة مطلقة) that actually lifts hadath until the permitter (water) occurs, so when water becomes available, it ends; for Shafi'i, it is a substitute that permits worship while hadath remains, so obtaining water does not terminate it mid-prayer.

Key Terms
قدرة ماء (qudrat ma'): Ability to obtain water (surplus to one's needs) that can be used for purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person performs tayammum and starts praying, then during the prayer he obtains water and is able to use it, what happens?
A) The prayer continues validly.
B) The tayammum is nullified and the prayer becomes invalid.
C) The prayer becomes makruh but still valid.
D) He must stop and perform istinja.

Key Takeaway
Ability to obtain water is the key condition for tayammum; its presence invalidates tayammum immediately, even during prayer.

Delaying Prayer When Hoping for Water
Ruling on delaying prayer for hope of water and building upon with tayammum after wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi recommendation to delay prayer when hoping for water, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on its obligation, and analyze the ruling on building upon with tayammum after wudu.

Core Idea
One who hopes for water delays prayer to use water; building upon is allowed per Abu Hanifa.

This part of the passage deals with a person who lacks water but has strong hope of finding it before the prayer time ends. The Hanafi school recommends delaying the prayer to perform it with water, as this is better. However, there is a difference of opinion within the school on whether this delay is obligatory. Additionally, the passage discusses the case of 'building upon' when one starts with wudu, then loses it, and uses tayammum to continue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on delaying
The matn states that one who hopes for water delays the prayer. The commentator explains this is recommended (mustahab).
The hope must be a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann).
2
Note the scope and exceptions
The ruling includes delaying even Maghrib until twilight disappears, and applies to two obligatory prayers and fear of missing funeral or Eid prayers.
If no hope, the best is to pray at the beginning of the time.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some narrations from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf state that delaying is wajib because strong presumption is like actual finding.
The majority view is mustahab.
4
Understand the building scenario
If one begins prayer with wudu, then has hadath and hopes for water, he can perform tayammum and continue (build upon) his prayer according to Abu Hanifa.
The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require a fresh wudu and tayammum and restart.
5
Connect to the usul principle
The underlying difference is the nature of tayammum: Hanafi: absolute purification that lifts hadath until permitter found; Sahibayn: substitute that does not lift hadath fully.
This affects building upon and other rules.

(فتح المعين) وقدرة ماء: أشار به إلى أن الوجدان في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً﴾ (النساء: ٤٣) بمعنى القدرة، وعدل عن رؤية الماء إلى القدرة؛ لشمولها ما لو تيمم لبرد أو مرض، وخرج بها ما لو مرَّ النائم بصفة لا توجب النقض على ماء كاف حيث لا ينتقض تيممه. (فتح المعين) تمنع التيمم: يعني إذا كان قدرة الماء ناقض التيمم فتمنع التيمم ابتداءً وتنقضه انتهاءً مطلقاً، سواء كانت قدرته في الصلاة أو في غيرها، وقال الشافعي: لا يرفع التيمم إذا قدر على الماء بعد ما شرع في الصلاة؛ لأن حرمة الصلاة مانعة عن إبطالها، فكان عاجزاً عن الاستعمال حكماً، ولنا أنه قادر حقيقة فيبطل تيممه، ولا يبقى للصلاة حرمة لفوات شرطها؛ لأن التراب لم يجعل طهوراً إلا . عند عدم الماء فيبطل بوجوده. (فتح المعين) يؤخر الصلاة: أي يستحب لعادم الماء إذا غلب على رأيه القدرة عليه أن يؤخر الصلاة حتى يؤديه بأكمل الطهارتين، وظاهر إطلاقه يشمل صلاة المغرب، فيؤخر إلى غيبوبة الشفق وهو الذي عليه الأكثر، وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف في غير رواية الأصول أن التأخير واجب؛ لأن غلبة الرأي كالمتحقق وعن. مالك: المندوب أن في وسط الوقت، وإذا لم يرج الأفضل صلاة في أول الوقت اتفاقاً. (فتح المعين قبل الوقت إلخ: خلافاً للشافعي في تلك المسألتين والخلاف بيننا وبينه يبتني على أن التيمم عندنا طهارة مطلقة يرتفع به الحدث إلى وقت وجود مبيح مع قيام الحدث، وعنده بدل ضروري مبيح مع قيام الحدث حقيقة. (فتح المعين) ولو بناءً [ أي لو كانت صلاته بناء كما لو شرع فيها بالوضوء ثم سبقه حدث تيمم ييني خلافا لهما. (ط)] وقالا : يتيمم ويتوضأ ويتم صلاته، ولا خلاف في أنه إذا شرع بالتيمم يتيمم، وكذا لو شرع بالوضوء ثم أحدث ويخاف زوال الشمس إذا اشتغل بالوضوء تيمم اتفاقاً، فإن لم يخف ويرجو إدراك الإمام قبل الفراغ لم يتيمم إجماعاً. (مسكين)
And the ability to obtain water beyond his need prevents tayammum and nullifies it. And one who hopes for water delays the prayer, before the time, and for two obligatory prayers, and out of fear of missing a funeral prayer or Eid, even if it is a building upon. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Ability to obtain water': he indicated thereby that 'finding' in His statement 'then you did not find water' (4:43) means ability. He turned from seeing water to ability to include cases of tayammum due to cold or illness, and excluded cases where a sleeping person passes by a sufficient [؟] in a way that does not necessitate nullification, so his tayammum is not nullified. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Prevents tayammum': meaning that if ability to obtain water is a nullifier of tayammum, it prevents tayammum initially and nullifies it absolutely, whether his ability occurs during prayer or outside it. Al-Shafi'i said: it does not nullify tayammum if he obtains water after starting prayer, because the sanctity of prayer prevents its invalidation, so he is considered legally unable to use it. Our argument: he is actually able, so his tayammum becomes invalid, and the prayer loses its sanctity due to the loss of its condition, because dust was not made a purifier except in the absence of water, so it is invalidated by its presence. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Delays the prayer': i.e., it is recommended for one who lacks water, if he strongly thinks he can obtain it, to delay the prayer until he performs it with the better of the two purifications. The apparent scope includes the Maghrib prayer, so he delays until the disappearance of the twilight, which is the view of the majority. From Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, in non-riwayah al-usul, that delaying is obligatory, because strong presumption is like actuality. From Malik, it is recommended to pray in the middle of the time. If he does not hope, the best is to pray at the beginning of the time by agreement. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Before the time, etc.': contrary to al-Shafi'i in these two issues. The disagreement between us and him is based on the fact that tayammum in our view is an absolute purification that removes hadath until the time when a permitter is found while hadath remains; according to him, it is a necessary substitute that permits while hadath actually remains. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Even if it is building': that is, if his prayer is a building, as if he began with wudu then an event preceded him, he performs tayammum and builds, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The two said: he performs tayammum and wudu and completes his prayer. There is no disagreement that if he begins with tayammum, he performs tayammum. Similarly, if he begins with wudu then has hadath and fears the sun will set if he occupies himself with wudu, he performs tayammum by agreement. If he does not fear and hopes to catch the imam before finishing, he does not perform tayammum unanimously. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage deals with two related issues: the effect of ability to obtain water on tayammum, and the recommendation to delay prayer when hoping for water. The matn says that ability to obtain surplus water prevents performing tayammum initially and also nullifies an existing tayammum. The commentator explains that the Quranic term 'finding' (فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا) is interpreted as ability (قدرة), not mere sight, to include cases like cold or illness that prevent using water. He records a dispute with Shafi'i: Shafi'i says if one starts prayer with tayammum then obtains water, the prayer is valid and tayammum is not nullified because the prayer's sanctity prevents nullification; Hanafis argue that since one is actually able to use water, the tayammum becomes invalid and the prayer condition is lost. Regarding delaying prayer, the majority holds it is recommended (mustahab) for one who strongly suspects water will appear to delay until near the end of prayer time to perform with water; some narrations from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say it is wajib. The commentator also addresses the case of 'building upon' (ببناء) when one starts with wudu, then has hadath, and has hope of water—there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether he can combine tayammum and wudu. The key underlying principle is that for Hanafis, tayammum is an absolute purification (طهارة مطلقة) that actually lifts hadath until the permitter (water) occurs, so when water becomes available, it ends; for Shafi'i, it is a substitute that permits worship while hadath remains, so obtaining water does not terminate it mid-prayer.

Key Terms
راجي الماء (raji al-ma'): One who hopes to find water, having a strong presumption (غلبة الظن) of its availability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi opinion, what is the ruling for a person who strongly hopes to find water before the end of prayer time?
A) He must delay the prayer until he finds water.
B) It is recommended to delay the prayer.
C) He should pray immediately with tayammum.
D) He should combine prayers.

Key Takeaway
Delaying prayer for hope of water is recommended, not obligatory, and building upon with tayammum after wudu is allowed per Abu Hanifa.

Conditions and Nullifiers of Tayammum with Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Expansion of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on tayammum rulings and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid tayammum, identify what nullifies it (including the nuance for janabah), and explain the intra-Hanafi disputes on intention and apostasy.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires intention and inability to use water; apostasy does not nullify it, and its nullifiers mirror wudu with an exception for ghusl.

Tayammum is a substitute purification when water is unavailable. Its validity hinges on specific conditions, and there are important intramadhhab differences on whether intention is required (Abu Hanifa vs. Zufar) and whether apostasy nullifies it (Abu Hanifa vs. Zufar). This lesson unpacks the rulings and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and conditions
From the matn, tayammum is valid only when one is unable to use water and has intention. Note that 'inability' includes both inability to find water and inability to use it due to harm.
The commentator clarifies that intention is a condition (shart) for validity.
2
Examine the dispute on intention for tayammum
Zufar holds that intention is not a condition for tayammum, while Abu Hanifa requires it. The mufta bihi is the latter. Also, for wudu, Hanafis do not require intention, unlike Shafi'i.
This difference stems from the nature of tayammum as a substitute requiring conscious substitution.
3
Analyze the ruling on a disbeliever's tayammum
A disbeliever's tayammum for embracing Islam is valid; but for prayer it is invalid by consensus. This is because a disbeliever is not a person of prayer (ahl al-salah).
The commentator contrasts this with wudu, where Hanafis allow a disbeliever's wudu to be valid even without intention.
4
Understand the effect of apostasy on tayammum
According to Abu Hanifa, apostasy does not nullify tayammum. If a Muslim performs tayammum, then apostatizes, then returns, he remains on his tayammum. Zufar holds the opposite.
This is based on the view that tayammum is a substitute for water and continues to serve its purpose upon return.
5
Learn the nullifiers of tayammum
Everything that nullifies wudu also nullifies tayammum, except when tayammum was performed for ghusl (janabah): a minor hadath nullifies only the wudu aspect, not the ghusl aspect.
Hence, the commentator prefers saying 'nullifiers of the original (wudu/ghusl)' rather than just 'nullifiers of wudu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التيمم

وبه بلا عجز ناوياً، فلغا تيمم كافر لا وضوؤه، ولا ينقضه ردّة بل ناقض الوضوء، وقدرة ماء فضل عن حاجته فهي تمنع التيمم وترفعه وراجي الماء يؤخر الصلاة، قبل الوقت، ولفرضين وخوف فوت صلاة جنازة أو عيد ولو بناء . .

وصح التيمم أي وصح لأجل أي كل تكبيراتها ولو وليا بلا عجز عن التراب، وعند أبي يوسف يجوز عند العجز. (ط) ناوياً : أي يتيمم ناوياً استباحة الصلاة أو قربة لا تتأدى بلا طهارة، وعند زفر نيته ليست بشرط (ط) تيمم كافر للإسلام، وأما إذا تيمم للصلاة فلا يجوز بالاتفاق؛ لأن الكافر ليس من أهلها، وفي الوضوء خلاف الشافعي؛ لافتقاره إلى النية عنده، والكافر ليس من أهلها. (فتح) ولا ينقضه: أي إن توضأ الكافر للإسلام ثم أسلم فهو متوضئ خلافاً للشافعي ردّة: فلو تيمم مسلم ثم ارتد - والعياذ بالله - ثم أسلم فهو على تيممه خلافاً لزفر. (ط) بل ناقض الوضوء أي ينقضه ما ينقض الوضوء؛ لأنه خلفه، فيأخذ حكمه، ولو قال: ناقض الأصل ليعم الوضوء والغسل لكان أحسن؛ لأنه ليس كل ما ينقض الوضوء ينقض التيمم كما إذا تيمم لجنابة ثم عرضه الحدث الأصغر انتقض تيمم الوضوء دون تيمم الغسل. (فتح)
Chapter of Tayammum. And with it without inability, intending, then the tayammum of a disbeliever is invalid, not his ablution, and apostasy does not nullify it but rather nullifiers of wudu, and possession of water surplus to his need prevents tayammum and raises it, and one who hopes for water delays prayer, before the time, and for two obligatory prayers and fear of missing a funeral or Eid prayer, even if it is a building. And the validity of tayammum: it is valid for the sake of any of its takbirs even if delayed, without inability to use earth. According to Abu Yusuf, it is permissible when unable. (T) Intending: he performs tayammum intending to permit prayer or an act of worship that cannot be performed without purity. According to Zufar, intention is not a condition. (T) The tayammum of a disbeliever for embracing Islam; but if he performs tayammum for prayer, it is not permissible by consensus because the disbeliever is not of its people. Regarding wudu, there is disagreement with al-Shafi'i because he requires intention, and the disbeliever is not of its people. (Fath) And it does not nullify it: i.e., if the disbeliever performs wudu for Islam and then becomes Muslim, he is in a state of wudu, contrary to al-Shafi'i. Apostasy: if a Muslim performs tayammum then apostatizes and then returns to Islam, he remains on his tayammum, contrary to Zufar. (T) Rather, nullifiers of wudu: what nullifies wudu nullifies it because it is its substitute, so it takes its ruling. If he said: nullifiers of the original to include wudu and ghusl, it would be better, because not everything that nullifies wudu nullifies tayammum, as when he performs tayammum for janabah then a minor hadath occurs, the tayammum for wudu is nullified but not the tayammum for ghusl. (Fath)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the chapter of tayammum. It opens with the core ruling: tayammum is performed when one is unable to use water, and it requires intention (niyyah). The commentator then addresses several important issues: (1) The tayammum of a disbeliever is only valid if performed specifically for the purpose of embracing Islam; if done for prayer, it is invalid by consensus. This is because the disbeliever is not considered a person of prayer (ahl al-salah). However, there is a difference with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding wudu, as he requires intention for wudu, and the disbeliever's intention is not valid. (2) Apostasy does not nullify tayammum according to Abu Hanifa, unlike Zufar. (3) What nullifies wudu also nullifies tayammum because tayammum is a substitute (khalaf). However, the commentator notes an important nuance: if one performs tayammum for janabah (major impurity) and then experiences a minor hadath (e.g., passing wind), the tayammum for wudu is nullified, but the tayammum for ghusl remains valid. This is because the minor hadath only affects the wudu, not the ghusl. The commentator thus prefers the phrase 'nullifiers of the original' to cover both wudu and ghusl. This passage includes intra-Hanafi disputes with Abu Yusuf (who allows tayammum when unable to use earth) and Zufar (who does not require intention). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that intention is required and inability to use water or earth is necessary.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Ritual purification using clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful
نيّة (niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform tayammum for the purpose of permitting prayer or an act of worship that requires purity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the tayammum of a disbeliever who intends to embrace Islam?
A) It is valid.
B) It is invalid because a disbeliever cannot have intention.
C) It is valid only if done at the direction of a Muslim.
D) It is invalid by consensus.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum requires intention and inability to use water; intra-Hanafi disputes exist on intention and apostasy, but the mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa requiring intention and denying nullification by apostasy.

Meaning of Qadra Ma' and Its Effect on Tayammum
Dispute on nullification of tayammum upon ability to water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum nullification upon gaining ability to water and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Tayammum is nullified by mere ability to use water — even during prayer — because earth is a purifier only when water is absent.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its commentary explains a critical concept: that the Quranic term 'finding water' (wijdan) means ability to use it, not mere visual perception. This interpretation has a direct practical impact: if one gains ability to water after performing tayammum, the tayammum is nullified, even if that happens during prayer. The passage then presents the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response, giving us a classic example of an ikhtilaf rooted in usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term and its interpretation
The commentator explains that 'qadra ma'' refers to the ability to use water. This is derived from the Quranic 'wijdan' in verse 4:43, which the Hanafis interpret as 'qudra' (ability) rather than simply seeing water.
2
State the Hanafi position on tayammum nullification
Hanafis hold that ability to water (qadra) prevents tayammum initially and nullifies it absolutely if it occurs later, whether or not one is in prayer.
3
Present the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i argues that the inviolability (hurma) of prayer prevents nullification of tayammum once prayer has started, making the person legally unable to use water.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal is that the person is truly able (qadir haqiqatan), so the tayammum is invalidated. The prayer has no inviolability because its condition (tahara with water) is lost.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafi: one must stop praying, perform wudu/ghusl, and repeat the prayer. Shafi'i: the prayer continues valid and need not be repeated.
This difference shows how usul interpretation directly affects daily practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقدرة ماء: أشار به إلى أن الوجدان في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً﴾ (النساء: ٤٣) بمعنى القدرة، وعدل عن رؤية الماء إلى القدرة؛ لشمولها ما لو تيمم لبرد أو مرض، وخرج بها ما لو مرَّ النائم بصفة لا توجب النقض على ماء كاف حيث لا ينتقض تيممه. (فتح المعين)

تمنع التيمم: يعني إذا كان قدرة الماء ناقض التيمم فتمنع التيمم ابتداءً وتنقضه انتهاءً مطلقاً، سواء كانت قدرته في الصلاة أو في غيرها، وقال الشافعي: لا يرفع التيمم إذا قدر على الماء بعد ما شرع في الصلاة؛ لأن حرمة الصلاة مانعة عن إبطالها، فكان عاجزاً عن الاستعمال حكماً، ولنا أنه قادر حقيقة فيبطل تيممه، ولا يبقى للصلاة حرمة لفوات شرطها؛ لأن التراب لم يجعل طهوراً إلا عند عدم الماء فيبطل بوجوده. (فتح المعين)
And possession of water: it indicates that the term 'finding' in His statement: {And you do not find water} (al-Nisa:43) means ability (qudra). He turned from seeing water to ability to include the case of tayammum due to cold or illness, and by it is excluded the case of one passing by a well but not needing to draw water because his tayammum is not nullified. (Fath al-Mu'in) It prevents tayammum: it means that if ability to water is a nullifier of tayammum, it prevents tayammum initially and nullifies it conclusively absolutely, whether his ability occurs during prayer or outside of it. Al-Shafi'i said: It does not raise tayammum if he gains ability to water after starting the prayer because the inviolability of prayer prevents its nullification, so he is considered legally unable. Our proof: He is truly able, so his tayammum is invalidated, and the prayer has no inviolability due to the loss of its condition, because earth was not made a purifier except when water is absent, so it is nullified by its existence. (Fath al-Mu'in)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage expands on the matn phrase 'qadra ma'' (ability to access water). The commentator explains that the Quranic word 'finding' (wijdan) in verse 4:43 is interpreted as 'ability' (qudra) rather than mere seeing. This is a crucial usul point: the absence of water that permits tayammum is assessed by one's ability to use it, not by its mere presence. For example, if one sees water but cannot use it due to cold, illness, or lack of a vessel, tayammum is valid. Conversely, if one passes by a well but has no need to draw water, his tayammum remains valid. The main point of dispute with al-Shafi'i is whether tayammum is nullified if one gains ability to water after having started prayer. The Hanafi position is that it is nullified absolutely, even during prayer, because the condition for tayammum (absence of water) has ceased. Al-Shafi'i argues that the sanctity of the prayer (hurmat al-salah) prevents its nullification, making the person legally unable. The Hanafi response is that the prayer's condition (tahara with water) is no longer met, so the prayer itself is invalid, and its sanctity cannot be maintained without the condition. The Hanafi view is that earth (turab) is only a purifier in the absence of water; thus, with the presence of water, the tayammum is automatically nullified.

Key Terms
قدرة ماء (qadra ma'): The ability to access and use water, either by having it at hand or being able to obtain it without harm or difficulty
الوجدان (al-wijdan): The Quranic term for 'finding' water, interpreted by Hanafis as 'ability' (qudra) rather than mere visual perception

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs tayammum and then during prayer sees water but cannot leave the prayer to fetch it, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The tayammum is nullified and the prayer is invalid.
B) The prayer continues validly because the person cannot use the water.
C) The prayer is valid but must be repeated later.
D) The tayammum remains valid because seeing water does not nullify it.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mere ability to access and use water nullifies tayammum, regardless of whether one actually uses it or is in prayer.

Delaying Prayer for Hope of Water and the Building (Bina') Ruling
Ruling on delaying prayer and the permissibility of building on a prayer after tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying prayer when hoping for water and explain the intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab dispute on building (bina') after hadath, citing the underlying usul difference on the nature of tayammum.

Core Idea
Delaying prayer for hope of water is recommended; building on a prayer after tayammum is allowed per Abu Hanifa.

When a person is without water but has a strong presumption of finding it later, should he delay the prayer to perform it with water? This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses that question and also tackles a related controversy: if a person starts prayer with wudu, then experiences hadath, can he simply perform tayammum and continue the same prayer? The answers hinge on the Hanafi understanding of tayammum as an absolute purification (tahara mutlaqa) versus a mere permit (mubih). Let's walk through the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on delaying prayer
Determine the hukm (legal classification) for delaying prayer when one has a strong presumption (ghalabat al-ra'y) of finding water. The majority view is mustahab, but a narration makes it wajib.
The source text states: 'وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف في غير رواية الأصول أن التأخير واجب'
2
Understand the scope of delay for Maghrib
Note that the ruling applies to all prayers, including Maghrib, and the recommended delay extends until the disappearance of the twilight (shafaq).
There is also a Maliki view suggesting praying in the middle of the time.
3
Analyze the building (bina') dispute
If one starts prayer with wudu, then hadath occurs, Abu Hanifa allows tayammum and building (continuing) the prayer. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require a fresh start with both wudu and tayammum.
The disagreement stems from whether tayammum raises hadath (tahara mutlaqa) or merely permits worship (mubih).
4
Identify consensus exceptions
There is consensus that if one started with tayammum and then hadath occurs, he simply repeats tayammum without wudu. Also, if one fears missing the sun (e.g., for Fajr) or losing the congregation, he does tayammum by agreement.
This shows the practical limits of the dispute.
5
Connect to the cross-madhhab usul
The Shafi'i school rejects building because tayammum does not remove hadath; it only permits worship. The Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa) considers tayammum an absolute purification that removes hadath temporarily.
This usul difference (tahara mutlaqa vs. mubih) is the root of the building dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يؤخر الصلاة: أي يستحب لعادم الماء إذا غلب على رأيه القدرة عليه أن يؤخر الصلاة حتى يؤديه بأكمل الطهارتين، وظاهر إطلاقه يشمل صلاة المغرب، فيؤخر إلى غيبوبة الشفق وهو الذي عليه الأكثر، وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف في غير رواية الأصول أن التأخير واجب؛ لأن غلبة الرأي كالمتحقق وعن. مالك: المندوب أن في وسط الوقت، وإذا لم يرج الأفضل صلاة في أول الوقت اتفاقاً. (فتح المعين قبل الوقت إلخ: خلافاً للشافعي في تلك المسألتين والخلاف بيننا وبينه يبتني على أن التيمم عندنا طهارة مطلقة يرتفع به الحدث إلى وقت وجود مبيح مع قيام الحدث، وعنده بدل ضروري مبيح مع قيام الحدث حقيقة. (فتح المعين) ولو بناءً [ أي لو كانت صلاته بناء كما لو شرع فيها بالوضوء ثم سبقه حدث تيمم ييني خلافا لهما. (ط)] وقالا : يتيمم ويتوضأ ويتم صلاته، ولا خلاف في أنه إذا شرع بالتيمم يتيمم، وكذا لو شرع بالوضوء ثم أحدث ويخاف زوال الشمس إذا اشتغل بالوضوء تيمم اتفاقاً، فإن لم يخف ويرجو إدراك الإمام قبل الفراغ لم يتيمم إجماعاً. (مسكين)
He delays the prayer: i.e., it is recommended for one without water, if he has a strong impression that he will gain ability to water, to delay the prayer so that he may perform it with the more complete of the two purifications. Its apparent generality includes the Maghrib prayer, so he delays it until the disappearance of the twilight (shafaq), and this is the view of the majority. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in a non-principle narration, delaying is obligatory because a strong impression is like certainty. According to Malik, the recommended is in the middle of the time. If he does not hope, it is better to pray at the beginning of the time by agreement. (Fath al-Mu'in) Before the time etc.: contrary to al-Shafi'i in these two issues. The difference between us and him is based on the fact that tayammum with us is an absolute purification (tahara mutlaqa) by which the state of hadath is removed until the time of the existence of the permitting factor, while the hadath subsists; with him it is a necessary substitute that permits while the hadath really subsists. (Fath al-Mu'in) And even if it is building: i.e., if his prayer is a building as in when he starts it with wudu then a hadath precedes him, he performs tayammum and builds, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). (T) They said: he performs tayammum and wudu and completes his prayer. There is no disagreement that if he started with tayammum, he does tayammum; likewise if he started with wudu then hadath and fears the sun will set if he occupies himself with wudu, he does tayammum by agreement. If he does not fear and hopes to catch the imam before he finishes, he does not do tayammum by consensus. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage addresses the recommendation to delay prayer for one who is confident (ghalaba 'ala ra'yihi) that he will find water later. The ruling is that it is mustahab (recommended) to delay, so that the prayer can be performed with the more complete purity (water). The majority opinion includes Maghrib prayer, delaying until the redness disappears. However, there is a narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that delaying is wajib (obligatory) because strong presumption is treated as certainty. There is also a view from Malik that it is recommended to pray in the middle of the time. If there is no hope, it is better to pray early by agreement. The passage also addresses the concept of 'building' (bina') in prayer: if one starts prayer with wudu and then hadath occurs, can he build on that prayer by performing tayammum and then continuing? The Hanafi school has a split: Abu Hanifa allows building, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he must perform tayammum and wudu (i.e., start anew). The commentator notes that if he started the prayer with tayammum, he obviously does tayammum on hadath. If he started with wudu and then hadath and fears losing the sun (for Fajr?), he does tayammum by agreement. If no fear, and he hopes to catch the congregation, he does not do tayammum by consensus. The underlying principle: in the Hanafi school, tayammum is considered an absolute purification that raises the hadath, while for Shafi'i it is a mere substitute that allows worship while hadath remains. This affects whether one can build on a prayer started with tayammum after hadath occurs.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): Building (continuing) a prayer after a disruption (e.g., hadath) by performing tayammum without restarting the entire prayer
غلبة الرأي (ghalabat al-ra'y): A strong presumption or dominant opinion that one will find water, sufficient to justify delaying prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what is the ruling on delaying the Maghrib prayer for one who hopes to find water?
A) It is obligatory to delay until the twilight disappears.
B) It is recommended to delay until the twilight disappears.
C) It is prohibited to delay.
D) It is recommended to delay only until the middle of the time.

Key Takeaway
Delaying prayer for hope of water is recommended, not obligatory; building on a prayer after tayammum is allowed according to Abu Hanifa, reflecting the Hanafi view of tayammum as a full purification.

Taharah — Purification

Tayammum: Method, Valid Earth, and Inter-Madhhab Disputes
Inter-madhhab dispute on the valid earth and method of tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of tayammum, identify the pillars and conditions, and evaluate the madhhab dispute over the valid type of earth.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires pure earth from its genus, two strikes, and full coverage; the meaning of 'tayyib' divides schools.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi method of tayammum as presented in the matn and elaborated by the commentator. The passage details the obligatory acts (arkan), the conditions (shurut), and the recommended sequence. It also addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: what qualifies as 'pure earth' (sa'id tayyib)? The Hanafi school adopts a broad definition, while al-Shafi'i restricts it to fertile soil. Understanding the linguistic and usul principles behind this difference sharpens your fiqh reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on the method
From the matn and commentary, extract the required actions: two strikes, full coverage of face and arms including elbows, and the type of earth.
The matn says 'with two strikes' and 'covering his face and his arms together with his elbows'.
2
Analyze the pillars and conditions
List the two pillars (rukn: two strikes and isti'ba') and the six conditions mentioned in the commentary.
Conditions include intention, wiping with ≥3 fingers, pure earth (sa'id), purifying earth, absence of water.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference on isti'ba'
Note the narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad that full coverage is not required; the zahir riwayah requires it.
The commentator states the correct view is full coverage and fatwa is upon it.
4
Trace the madhhab dispute on the type of earth
State the Hanafi position (any pure earth from jins al-ard), the Shafi'i position (only munbit), and Abu Yusuf's view (only dust/sand). Identify the key proof: Quran 4:43 and the interpretation of 'tayyib'.
Hanafi argues 'tayyib' is a homonym; here it means 'pure' by consensus.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Consider a scenario: a traveler has only a stone or lime. Hanafi permits tayammum; Shafi'i does not. What effect does this have on prayer validity?
This difference leads to real-world differences in where and when tayammum is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستوعباً وجهه ويديه مع مرفقيه بضربتين، ولو جنبا أو حائضا، بطاهر من جنس الأرض وإن لم يكن عليه نقع، إذا طهرت من الحيض

على جنس الأرض عدو: يمنعه أو يخاف على نفسه الهلاك أو الحبس، أو على ماله منه، أو على نفسه من فاسق عند الماء. (ط) أو عطش: على نفسه أو دابته ولو كلباً، وكذا لو احتاجه لعجن. (ط) أو فقد آلة يعني رأى الماء وليس معه آلة الاستسقاء أي طاهرة، ولو لم يجد آلة يستسقي بها ووجد من ينزل إلى الماء بأجر لزمه. (الدر المختار) مستوعباً: ا حال من المستكن في "يتيمم" وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى، وروى الحسن عن الإمام أن الاستيعاب ليس بشرط، حتى لو مسح أكثر الذراعين والكف جاز، وعلى ظاهر الرواية لا يجوز، حتى لابد من نزع الخاتم والسوار وتخليل الأصابع، وبه يفتى. ملا مسكين مع مرفقيه فلو قطعت يداه من المرفق مسح موضع القطع، ولو فوق المرفق لا خلافا لزفر ، فإن عنده مسح محل القطع لا يلزمه وعند الشافعي إلى الرسغين في القديم، وفي الجديد كمذهبنا، وقال مالك وأحمد: مسح يديه إلى رسغيه والمشهور من مذهب مالك أن المسح إلى الرسغين فرض، وإلى المرفقين سنة، وعن الزهري إلى الإبط. (فتح المعين، الطائي) بضربتين [متعلق بـ"يتيمم" أو بــ"مستوعباً. (ع)] وكان ابن سيرين يقول بثلاث ضربات: ضربة في الوجه، وضربة في اليدين وضربة ثالثة فيهما، وعن مالك يكتفي بضربة واحدة وبه قال أحمد في رواية، وعندنا: ضربتان ضربة للوجه، وضربة لليدين؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لعمار بن ياسر : يكفيك ضربة للوجه، وضربة للذراعين"، وكيفية التيمم أن يضرب يديه على جنس الأرض ويمسح بهما وجهه، ثم يضرب ضربة ثانية، ويضع بطن كفه اليسرى على ظهر كفه اليمني ويمسح بثلاثة أصابع - أي الخنصر وتالييه - ظاهر يده اليمني إلى المرفق ثم يمسح باطنه بالإبهام والمسبحة إلى رؤوس الأصابع، ثم يفعل باليسرى كذلك وركن التيمم: الضربتان والاستيعاب، وشروطه ستة: النية والمسح وكونه بثلاثة أصابع وأكثر والصعيد وكونه مطهراً وفقد الماء، وزاد ابن حبان في الشروط الإسلام، وقد مرّ ببيان سننه الثمانية. (فتح، در المختار وغيره) بطاهر إلخ: لو أبدله بالطهور لكان أولى؛ احترازا عن الأرض المتنجسة بعد الجفاف تكون طاهرة في حق الصلاة دون التيمم، والجار والمجرور متعلق بـ"يتيمم" عند أكثر الشراح، لكن قال في العيني [٢٥/١]: هو صفة الضربتين، أي بضربتين المتصفتين بطاهر من جنس الأرض، كالتراب والرمل والحجر والنورة والزرنيخ والكحل، وقال أبو يوسف لا يجوز إلا بالتراب والرمل خاصة، وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز إلا بالتراب المنبت؛ لقوله تعالى: صَعِيداً طيبا (النساء:٤٣) أي ترابا منبتاً، ولنا أن الطيب اسم مشترك يراد به المنبت، ویراد به الطاهر، ويراد به الحلال، وههنا الطاهر مراد بالإجماع، فلا يكون غيره مراداً؛ إذ المشترك لا عموم له، واحترز به عما ليس من جنس الأرض، وهو ما يحترق بالنار فيصير رماداً كالشجر والحنطة، أو ينطبع ويلين كالحديد والرصاص والنقدين، أما إذا اغبر ما ليس من جنس الأرض فيجوز التيمم. (فتح وغيره)
Covering his face and his arms together with his elbows with two strikes, even if he is junub or menstruating, with pure (earth) of the genus of earth, even if there is no dust on it. When she is pure from menses. On the genus of earth: enemy: prevents him or he fears destruction, imprisonment, or loss of wealth from him, or from a transgressor at the water. (T) Or thirst: for himself or his riding animal even if a dog, likewise if he needs it for dough. (T) Or loss of means: he sees water but has no means to draw it, i.e., pure means. If he cannot find means to draw water but finds someone who can descend into the water for a fee, it is incumbent on him. (al-Durr al-Mukhtar) Covering: a state derived from the implicit subject in 'he performs tayammum' and it is the correct view and the fatwa is upon it. Al-Hasan narrated from the Imam that covering is not a condition, such that if he wipes most of the forearms and palm, it is permissible. According to the apparent transmission, it is not permissible, so he must remove the ring, bracelet, and interlace the fingers, and this is given fatwa. With his elbows: if his hands are cut off at the elbow, he wipes the place of the cut; if above the elbow, no wiping is required, unlike Zufar, because according to him, wiping the cut site is not necessary. According to al-Shafi'i, it is to the wrists in the old view, in the new view like our school. Malik and Ahmad said: wiping the hands to the wrists, and the well-known from the school of Malik is that wiping to the wrists is obligatory, and to the elbows is sunna. From al-Zuhri: to the armpits. (Fath al-Mu'in, al-Ta'i) With two strikes: attached to 'he performs tayammum' or to 'covering'. Ibn Sirin used to say with three strikes: one strike for the face, one for the hands, and a third for them. Malik is reported to suffice with one strike, and Ahmad in one narration. According to us: two strikes—one for the face and one for the hands; due to his statement (peace be upon him) to 'Ammar ibn Yasir: 'Two strikes suffice you: one for the face and one for the forearms.' The manner of tayammum is that he strikes his hands on the genus of earth and wipes his face with them, then strikes a second time, and places the palm of his left hand on the back of his right hand and wipes with three fingers—the little finger and the two next to it—the outer part of his right arm to the elbow, then wipes the inner part with the thumb and index finger to the tips of the fingers, then does likewise with the left. The pillars (arkan) of tayammum are the two strikes and covering. Its conditions are six: intention, wiping, being with three fingers or more, the use of pure earth (sa'id), that it be pure (mutahhir), and absence of water. Ibn Hibban added Islam as a condition. The explanation of its eight sunnas has passed. (Fath, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, etc.) With pure etc.: if he replaced it with 'tahur' (purifier) it would be better; as a precaution against impure earth that after drying becomes pure for prayer but not for tayammum. The prepositional phrase is attached to 'he performs tayammum' according to most commentators, but al-'Ayni said it is a description of the two strikes, i.e., two strikes described as being with pure earth of the genus of earth, such as dust, sand, stone, lime, arsenic, and kohl. Abu Yusuf said: it is only permissible with dust and sand specifically. Al-Shafi'i said: it is only permissible with earth that grows plants (munbit), due to His statement: {sa'idan tayyiban} (al-Nisa:43), meaning earth that grows plants. Our proof: 'tayyib' is a homonym used for 'growing plants', 'pure', and 'lawful'; here 'pure' is intended by consensus, so nothing else is intended, because a homonym does not have generality. By it is excluded what is not of the genus of earth, which is what burns with fire and becomes ash like wood and wheat, or melts and softens like iron, lead, and the two precious metals (gold and silver). If something not of the genus of earth becomes dusty, tayammum is permissible. (Fath and others)
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed description of the method of tayammum and the conditions of the earth used. The matn states that one must wipe the entire face and arms including the elbows with two strikes. The commentator explains that covering (isti'ba') the entire area is the correct view and the basis for fatwa. However, there is a narration from al-Hasan (presumably al-Hasan ibn Ziyad) from the Imam (Abu Hanifa) that covering is not a condition—it suffices to wipe most of the forearms and palm. But the apparent (zahir) transmission from Abu Hanifa requires full coverage, including removing rings and bracelets and interlocking fingers. The passage also addresses various scenarios: if one fears an enemy, thirst, or lacks the means to draw water, these are valid excuses for tayammum. The method involves two strikes: one for the face, one for the arms. The hadith of 'Ammar ibn Yasir is cited as proof. The commentary then details the recommended way: after the first strike, wipe the face; after the second, wipe the right arm with three fingers (pinky, ring, middle) on the outer part and the thumb and index on the inner part, then the left. The pillars (arkan) are the two strikes and full coverage (isti'ba'). There are six conditions: intention, wiping (with the hand), using at least three fingers, using sa'id (pure earth), that the earth be purifying (mutahhir), and absence of water. Ibn Hibban added Islam. The commentator then discusses the requirement that the earth be pure (tahir) and of the genus of earth. Abu Yusuf restricted it to dust and sand; Shafi'i restricted to earth that grows plants (based on 'tayyib' meaning fertile). The Hanafi response is that 'tayyib' is a homonym and here it means 'pure' by consensus, so any pure earth from the genus of earth is valid. Examples include sand, stone, lime, etc. Substances that burn to ash or melt are not valid unless they become dusty.

Key Terms
ضربتان (darbatan): The two strikes of the hands on the earth for tayammum: one for the face and one for the arms
استيعاب (isti'ba'): The complete coverage of the face and arms during tayammum, ensuring that no part is left unwiped
صعيد (sa'id): The surface of the earth; any pure substance from the genus of earth used for tayammum

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a valid substance for tayammum?
A) Dust (turab)
B) Sand (raml)
C) Wood ash (ramad al-khashab)
D) Stone (hajar)

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is valid on any pure substance from the genus of earth, performed by two strikes covering the entire face and arms to the elbows, with full coverage (isti'ba') being a pillar.

Taharah — Purification

Valid Causes for Tayammum: Enemy, Beast, Thirst, and Lack of Vessel
States the reasons that permit tayammum and their conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four causes that permit tayammum and identify the condition for each cause that makes tayammum valid.

Core Idea
Tayammum is permitted not only when water is absent, but also when water is present but dangerous or inaccessible.

You may know that tayammum replaces wudu when no water is found. But the Hanafi school recognizes several situations where water is present yet tayammum is still allowed. In this passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, the mujtahid enumerates four causes: an enemy, a wild beast, thirst, and lack of a vessel. Each cause has a specific condition that must be met. Let us examine them closely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first cause: enemy
The enemy prevents access to water or causes fear for life, property, or even fear of a fasiq (sinner) at the water source. The key is the presence of fear or prevention.
Hanafis include fear of a fasiq, unlike Shafi'is.
2
Identify the second cause: wild beast
A wild beast (sabuʿ) that causes fear for life or property permits tayammum. The text does not specify additional conditions for this cause.
The presence of the beast itself justifies tayammum.
3
Identify the third cause: thirst
Thirst for oneself, one's riding animal (even a dog), or even need for kneading dough permits tayammum. The water is preserved for essential drinking or use.
The text explicitly includes a dog's thirst.
4
Identify the fourth cause: lack of vessel
Lack of a vessel (faqd al-ala) to draw water. If one can hire someone to fetch water for a fair wage, tayammum is not allowed. Only when hiring is impossible does this cause apply.
This condition prevents misuse of the dispensation.
5
Note the general conditions of tayammum
The passage also mentions that tayammum is performed with two strikes on pure earth, covering the face and arms to the elbows. This is valid even if no dust remains on the hands.
These are the pillars of tayammum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التيمم زك دت عدو أو سبع أو عطش، أو فقد آلة، مستوعباً وجهه ويديه مع مرفقيه بضربتين، ولو جنبا أو حائضا، بطاهر من جنس الأرض وإن لم يكن عليه نقع، إذا طهرت من الحيض على جنس الأرض عدو: يمنعه أو يخاف على نفسه الهلاك أو الحبس، أو على ماله منه، أو على نفسه من فاسق عند الماء. (ط) أو عطش: على نفسه أو دابته ولو كلباً، وكذا لو احتاجه لعجن. (ط) أو فقد آلة يعني رأى الماء وليس معه آلة الاستسقاء أي طاهرة، ولو لم يجد آلة يستسقي بها ووجد من ينزل إلى الماء بأجر لزمه. (الدر المختار)
Chapter of Tayammum: [Due to] an enemy, or a wild beast, or thirst, or lack of a vessel, covering his face and his arms along with his elbows with two strikes, even if he is junub or menstruating, with pure earth from the genus of earth even if there is no dust upon it, when she becomes pure from menstruation. On the genus of earth: an enemy: he prevents him or he fears destruction or imprisonment for himself, or for his property from it, or for himself from a transgressor at the water. (T) Or thirst: for himself or his riding animal, even if it is a dog, and likewise if he needs it for kneading dough. (T) Or lack of a vessel: meaning he sees water but does not have a vessel for drawing it, i.e., pure, and if he does not find a vessel to draw with and finds someone who can descend into the water for a fee, it becomes obligatory for him (to pay). (Al-Durr al-Mukhtar)
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage lists the permissible excuses for performing tayammum instead of wudu. The first set includes: (1) an enemy who prevents access to water or causes fear for life, property (including fear of a sinful person at the water source); (2) a wild beast causing fear; (3) thirst – either for oneself or one's riding animal, even if it is a dog, and even if the water is needed for kneading dough; (4) lack of a vessel (like a bucket or rope) to draw water – if one can hire someone to fetch water for a reasonable fee, then tayammum is not allowed. The text also mentions that tayammum is performed with two strikes covering the face and arms to the elbows, and that it is valid with pure earth even if no visible dust remains after striking. There is a brief note about a woman after menstruation, indicating that she must wait until she is pure (i.e., after her period ends) before tayammum becomes relevant for her. The (T) likely marks textual additions from a commentary like al-Ta'i.

Key Terms
العدو (al-aduww): An enemy who prevents access to water or causes fear for oneself or one's property.
فقد الآلة (faqd al-alah): Lack of a vessel or tool to draw water from a source.
السبع (al-sabu‘): A wild beast that causes fear for life or property.
العطش (al-atash): Thirst for oneself or one's animal, including a dog, or need for water for kneading dough.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A person is prevented from reaching water by an enemy.
B) A person sees water but has no cup and cannot afford to hire anyone.
C) A person has water but refuses to use it because he dislikes the taste.
D) A person fears a wild beast near the water.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is a dispensation granted in specific situations where water is present but accessing it is dangerous, impractical, or would cause harm.

Manner of Performing Tayammum and Its Rulings
Detailed method of tayammum with rulings and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the pillars and conditions of tayammum according to the Hanafi school, explain the intra-madhhab dispute regarding complete coverage (istighraq), and identify the dalil for two strikes.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires two strikes and full coverage of face and arms; omission of a pillar invalidates it.

This lesson examines the precise method of performing tayammum as outlined in Kanz al-Daqa'iq. We will explore the required elements, the reliance on the hadith of 'Ammar ibn Yasir, and the variance within the Hanafi school and with other madhhabs over the necessity of full coverage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tayammum is a substitute for wudu when water is unavailable. Its pillars (arkan) are the two strikes and complete coverage (istighraq) of face and arms to the elbows. Omission of any pillar invalidates tayammum.
The act is wajib for those with a valid excuse; the pillars are required for validity.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith of 'Ammar ibn Yasir: 'Two strokes suffice you: one for the face and one for the forearms.' This establishes the number of strikes and the body parts.
The dalil is a hadith ahad, making its transmission zannī, but it is acted upon due to practical necessity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit instruction 'يكفيك ضربة للوجه، وضربة للذراعين' indicates both the count (two) and the extent (face and forearms). The word 'يكفيك' implies sufficiency, reinforcing the obligatory nature.
Hanafi usul holds that the imperative (amr) here indicates wujub.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that Abu Hanifa did not require istighraq; wiping most of the arms sufficed. However, the mufta bihi is the zahir al-riwayah requiring full coverage.
The fatwa is on the stricter view to ensure certainty.
5
Evaluate the inter-madhhab differences
Other schools vary: Shafi'i's old view limits to wrists, Malik and Ahmad to wrists, Zufar exempts stump wiping, Ibn Sirin holds three strikes, and Malik allows one strike. The Hanafi school adheres to two strikes and full coverage.
Understanding these differences helps in knowing the thamarah al-khilaf in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستوعباً: ا حال من المستكن في "يتيمم" وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى، وروى الحسن عن الإمام أن الاستيعاب ليس بشرط، حتى لو مسح أكثر الذراعين والكف جاز، وعلى ظاهر الرواية لا يجوز، حتى لابد من نزع الخاتم والسوار وتخليل الأصابع، وبه يفتى. ملا مسكين مع مرفقيه فلو قطعت يداه من المرفق مسح موضع القطع، ولو فوق المرفق لا خلافا لزفر ، فإن عنده مسح محل القطع لا يلزمه وعند الشافعي إلى الرسغين في القديم، وفي الجديد كمذهبنا، وقال مالك وأحمد: مسح يديه إلى رسغيه والمشهور من مذهب مالك أن المسح إلى الرسغين فرض، وإلى المرفقين سنة، وعن الزهري إلى الإبط. (فتح المعين، الطائي) بضربتين [متعلق بـ"يتيمم" أو بــ"مستوعباً. (ع)] وكان ابن سيرين يقول بثلاث ضربات: ضربة في الوجه، وضربة في اليدين وضربة ثالثة فيهما، وعن مالك يكتفي بضربة واحدة وبه قال أحمد في رواية، وعندنا: ضربتان ضربة للوجه، وضربة لليدين؛ لقوله عليها لعمار بن ياسر : يكفيك ضربة للوجه، وضربة للذراعين"، وكيفية التيمم أن يضرب يديه على جنس الأرض ويمسح بهما وجهه، ثم يضرب ضربة ثانية، ويضع بطن كفه اليسرى على ظهر كفه اليمني ويمسح بثلاثة أصابع - أي الخنصر وتالييه - ظاهر يده اليمني إلى المرفق ثم يمسح باطنه بالإبهام والمسبحة إلى رؤوس الأصابع، ثم يفعل باليسرى كذلك وركن التيمم: الضربتان والاستيعاب، وشروطه ستة: النية والمسح وكونه بثلاثة أصابع وأكثر والصعيد وكونه مطهراً وفقد الماء، وزاد ابن حبان في الشروط الإسلام، وقد مرّ ببيان سننه الثمانية. (فتح، در المختار وغيره)
"Covering" (Musta'iban): it is a circumstantial accusative of the implicit subject in 'he performs tayammum' and that is the correct (view) and on it is the fatwa. Al-Hasan reported from the Imam (Abu Hanifa) that covering all (the parts) is not a condition, so if one wipes most of the forearms and the hand, it is permissible. But according to zahir al-riwayah it is not permissible, such that it is necessary to remove the ring and bracelet and to wipe between the fingers, and according to this (zahir al-riwayah) fatwa is given. "With his elbows": so if his hands are cut off at the elbow, he wipes the place of amputation. If (cut) above the elbow, there is no difference, but contrary to Zufar, who holds that wiping the amputation site is not required of him. According to al-Shafi'i: (wiping) to the wrists in the old (view), and in the new (view) it is like our madhhab. Malik and Ahmad said: he wipes his hands to the wrists, and the famous view from Malik's madhhab is that wiping to the wrists is fard, and to the elbows is sunnah. From al-Zuhri: to the armpit. (Fath al-Mu'in, al-Ta'i) "With two strikes" (bidarbatayn) is attached to 'he performs tayammum' or to 'covering'. (A) Ibn Sirin used to say with three strikes: one strike for the face, one for the hands, and a third for them (the hands) again. From Malik: he suffices with one strike, and Ahmad said so in one narration. According to us (Hanafis): two strikes: one for the face and one for the hands; because of his statement (peace be upon him) to 'Ammar ibn Yasir: "Two strokes suffice you: one for the face and one for the forearms." The manner of tayammum: he strikes his hands on pure earth and wipes his face with them, then strikes a second time, then places the inner palm of his left hand on the back of his right hand and wipes with three fingers (the little finger and the two next to it) the upper part of his right hand to the elbow, then wipes its inner part with the thumb and index finger to the fingertips. Then he does the same with the left. The pillars of tayammum are the two strikes and covering (all parts). Its conditions are six: intention, wiping, that it be with three fingers or more, pure earth (sa'id), that it be purifying, and unavailability of water. Ibn Hibban added Islam as a condition. The explanation of its eight sunan has preceded. (Fath, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, etc.)
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the precise method of performing tayammum, resolving disputes within the Hanafi school and with other madhhabs. The key issue is whether istighraq (complete covering) of the face and arms is required. The text states that the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that complete covering is necessary, and therefore one must remove rings and bracelets and wipe between the fingers. However, a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that Imam Abu Hanifa did not require complete coverage; only wiping most of the arms sufficed. Nevertheless, the fatwa is given on the 'zahir al-riwayah' position requiring full coverage. The passage then discusses amputation cases: if the hand is cut at the elbow, one wipes the stump; if above the elbow, the obligation remains to wipe whatever remains of the arm. There is a notable ikhtilaf with Zufar, who exempts wiping the stump entirely. The text compares the Hanafi view with Shafi'i (who limits wiping to the wrists in his old view but agreed with Hanafis later), Malik and Ahmad (who wipe to the wrists), and al-Zuhri (to the armpit). Regarding the number of strikes, the Hanafi school holds to two strikes based on the hadith of 'Ammar ibn Yasir, where the Prophet said two strokes suffice: one for the face and one for the forearms. The text describes the exact hand movements for the second strike: using the inner palm of the left hand on the back of the right, then wiping with three fingers (the little and adjacent ones) the outer part to the elbow, and then the inner part with the thumb and index finger to the fingertips, and similarly for the left hand. Finally, the pillars (arkan) are identified as the two strikes and complete coverage. The conditions are listed as six: intention, wiping (with the hands), that the wiping be with three fingers or more (so using the full hand is better), pure earth (sa'id), that the earth be purifying (not contaminated), and the unavailability of water. Ibn Hibban added Islam as a condition, but that is not part of the standard Hanafi conditions.

Key Terms
الاستيعاب (al-isti'ghraq): Complete coverage of the face and arms with the wipe during tayammum.
الضربتان (al-darbatan): The two strikes of the hands on pure earth, one for the face and one for the hands/arms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One strike
B) Two strikes
C) Three strikes
D) Four strikes

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates two strikes and complete coverage for tayammum, based on the hadith of 'Ammar and the zahir al-riwayah.

Permissible Earth for Tayammum: Hanafi Position and Disputes
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on permissible substances for tayammum, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the usul principle of mushtarak.

Core Idea
The Quranic term 'tayyib' is a homonym; Hanafis permit tayammum with any pure earth, Shafi'is restrict to vegetation-producing earth.

This passage defines 'pure earth' (sa'id tayyib) for tayammum, a point of dispute within the Hanafi school (Abu Yusuf) and between madhahib. By analyzing the Quranic verse and the usul concept of mushtarak (homonym), we understand how the Hanafi school derives a broader ruling. The practical consequence is that a traveler in a rocky desert can perform tayammum according to Hanafis, while Shafi'is require vegetation-growing earth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed condition
The ruling concerns what type of earth (sa'id) is valid for tayammum. The base text (Quduri) mentions 'with pure earth'. The dispute is about the meaning of 'pure'—does it mean any pure earth substance or only earth that grows plants?
2
Compare the positions
State the Hanafi majority position (any pure earth from the genus of earth: soil, sand, stone, lime, arsenic, kohl), Abu Yusuf's restriction (only soil and sand), and Imam al-Shafi'i's requirement (only vegetation-producing earth).
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Al-Shafi'i cites Quran 4:43 'sa'idan tayyiban' and interprets 'tayyib' as 'vegetation-producing' (munbit). This is based on the literal meaning of 'tayyib' in some contexts.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that 'tayyib' is a mushtarak (homonym) with multiple meanings: pure, lawful, vegetation-producing. By consensus (ijma) in this verse, it means 'pure'. Since a homonym does not convey all its meanings simultaneously (al-mushtarak la umum lahu), the agreed-upon meaning (pure) prevails.
This usul principle is key: a mushtarak cannot be used to argue for two different meanings at once.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a person is in a desert with only sand and stones, Hanafis allow tayammum; Shafi'is require the earth to be capable of growing plants, so tayammum would not be valid unless the earth is of that type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بطاهر إلخ: لو أبدله بالطهور لكان أولى؛ احترازا عن الأرض المتنجسة بعد الجفاف تكون طاهرة في حق الصلاة دون التيمم، والجار والمجرور متعلق بـ"يتيمم" عند أكثر الشراح، لكن قال في العيني [٢٥/١]: هو صفة الضربتين، أي بضربتين المتصفتين بطاهر من جنس الأرض، كالتراب والرمل والحجر والنورة والزرنيخ والكحل، وقال أبو يوسف لا يجوز إلا بالتراب والرمل خاصة، وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز إلا بالتراب المنبت؛ لقوله تعالى: صَعِيداً طيبا (النساء:٤٣) أي ترابا منبتاً، ولنا أن الطيب اسم مشترك يراد به المنبت، ویراد به الطاهر، ويراد به الحلال، وههنا الطاهر مراد بالإجماع، فلا يكون غيره مراداً؛ إذ المشترك لا عموم له، واحترز به عما ليس من جنس الأرض، وهو ما يحترق بالنار فيصير رماداً كالشجر والحنطة، أو ينطبع ويلين كالحديد والرصاص والنقدين، أما إذا اغبر ما ليس من جنس الأرض فيجوز التيمم. (فتح وغيره)
"With pure" etc.: If he had replaced it with 'purifying' it would have been better, to exclude contaminated earth that after drying is considered pure for prayer but not for tayammum. The prepositional phrase is attached to 'he performs tayammum' according to most commentators, but al-'Ayni said (1/25): it is a description of the two strikes, i.e., two strikes characterized by being from pure earth, such as soil, sand, stone, lime, arsenic, and kohl. Abu Yusuf said: it is not permissible except with soil and sand specifically. Al-Shafi'i said: it is not permissible except with earth that grows vegetation; due to His statement the Exalted: "Pure earth" (An-Nisa:43), meaning earth that grows vegetation. Our proof is that 'tayyib' is a homonym: it can mean vegetation-producing, pure, or lawful. Here, 'pure' is intended by consensus, so no other meaning is intended, because a homonym has no general application. And by this is excluded what is not from the genus of earth, which is what burns with fire and becomes ash like wood and wheat, or what melts and softens like iron, lead, and the two precious metals (gold and silver). However, if a non-earth substance becomes dusty, then tayammum is permissible. (Fath, etc.)
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage discusses the definition of 'pure earth' (sa'id tayyib) for tayammum, a point of intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab dispute. The text first clarifies that the phrase 'with pure earth' should ideally be 'with purifying earth' to exclude contaminated ground that has dried and is considered pure for salah but not for tayammum. Most commentators say the phrase modifies 'he performs tayammum', but al-'Ayni holds it describes the two strikes. The Hanafi school (majority view) allows tayammum with any substance from the genus of earth: soil, sand, stone, lime (nurah), arsenic (zarnikh), and kohl (antimony). Abu Yusuf restricts it to soil and sand only, while al-Shafi'i restricts it to earth that grows vegetation (al-turab al-munbit). The Shafi'i argument is based on the Quranic word 'tayyib' (pure) which they interpret as 'vegetation-producing'. The Hanafi response is that 'tayyib' is a homonym (mushtarak) that can mean pure, vegetation-producing, or lawful, and by consensus in this context it means pure. Since a homonym does not have general application (i.e., it does not carry all meanings simultaneously), only the intended meaning (pure) is valid. Excluded from 'earth' are things that burn to ash (like wood, wheat) or that melt and become pliable (like iron, lead, gold, silver). However, if such non-earth substances become dusty (e.g., powdered charcoal), then tayammum is allowed because the dust adheres to the hands.

Key Terms
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A word that has multiple meanings; here, 'tayyib' can mean pure, lawful, or vegetation-producing.
التراب المنبت (al-turab al-munbit): Earth that grows plants; required by Shafi'is for tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Lime

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tayammum with any pure earth substance, including stone and minerals, based on the Quranic term 'tayyib' being a mushtarak meaning pure by consensus.
