Wiping on the Outer Surface Only
Specifies that wiping is on the outer surface only.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the area of wiping during masḥ over leather socks, cite the evidence from the hadith of Ali, and explain the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Wiping is only on the outer (upper) surface of the khuff — the very act of the Prophet dictates the area.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a precise detail of masḥ over leather socks: exactly where on the sock is wiping valid? While common sense might suggest the inner sole is more deserving because it contacts impurity, the Hanafi school follows the explicit action of the Prophet, who wiped only the outer surface. The text presents the proof and then contrasts the Shafi'i/Maliki position that combines both surfaces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific ruling
Note that the obligatoriness of wiping is for the outer surface (zahir) of the khuff, not the inner (batin). This is the core statement of the passage.
The term 'shuri'a' implies legislation, making it a fixed obligation.
2
Recognize the primary proof
The hadith of Ali (ra) is cited: he saw the Prophet wiping only the outer surface with lines of his fingers. This is the evidentiary anchor for the Hanafi position.
The hadith challenges the logical assumption that the inner sole is more deserving.
3
Understand the opposing view
The text mentions that al-Shafi'i and Malik considered outer wiping as fard and inner as sunnah, based on other reports of the Prophet wiping both surfaces.
This introduces a cross-madhhab ikhtilaf.
4
Apply the ruling to different parts
The commentator elaborates that wiping on the front part of the outer surface is valid, but on the heel or above the ankle is not permissible. This sharpens the boundary of the defined area.
This shows practical application and prevents overgeneralization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على ظاهرهما: يعني إنما شرع المسح على ظاهرهما لا على باطنهما ؛ لقول علي رضي الله عنه: لو كان الدين بالرأي لكان باطن الخف أولى بالمسح من أعلاه، لكن رأيت رسول الله ﷺ يمسح على ظاهرهما خطوطا بالأصابع، وقال الشافعي ومالك على ظاهرهما فرض وعلى باطنهما سنة؛ لأنه عليه السلام مسح أعلى الخف وباطنه، وحديث رؤية عليّ لا ينافيه، فالأولى عند الشافعي: الجمع بين الأمرين بأن يضع يده اليمنى على ظاهر الخف الأيمن يعني فوقه، واليسرى على باطنه يعني تحته ويمسح ، ثم اليمنى تحت الخف الأيسر واليسرى فوقه ويمسح، ولو مسح على ما يلي الساق أو على ما يلي مقدم ظاهر الخف يجوز ، ولو مسح على العقب أو على ما فوق الكعبين لا يجوز. (فتح وغيره)
'On their outer surface': meaning, wiping is legislated on their outer surface, not on their inner surface, because of the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'If religion were by opinion, the inner part of the sock would be more deserving of wiping than the upper part, but I saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ wiping on their upper surface with lines of his fingers.' And al-Shafi'i and Malik said: wiping on the outer surface is fard, and on the inner is sunnah, because the Prophet ﷺ wiped the top and bottom of the sock, and the hadith of Ali's observation does not contradict that. According to al-Shafi'i, the better is to combine both by placing his right hand on the outer surface of the right sock (above) and his left hand on its inner surface (below) and wipe, then the right hand under the left sock and the left hand above it and wipe. If one wipes on that which is adjacent to the shin or on the front part of the outer surface, it is permissible. If one wipes on the heel or on what is above the ankles, it is not permissible. (Fath and others)
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the wiping must be on the outer (upper) surface of the leather socks, not on the inner side (the sole or underside). The evidence is the hadith of Ali (radiallahu 'anhu) who said that if religion were based on human reasoning, one would think the inner part is more deserving because it is the part that contacts impurity, but the Prophet ﷺ was seen wiping on the outer surface. This shows that the ruling is based on following the Sunnah, not rational analogy. The passage then mentions the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, which consider wiping on the outer surface as obligatory (fard) and on the inner surface as recommended (sunnah). They claim the Prophet ﷺ also wiped the inner part, so they combine both. The Hanafi response (implicitly in the text) rejects this, as the hadith of Ali only mentions the outer. The commentator then gives details: wiping on the part near the shin or on the front part of the outer surface is acceptable, but wiping on the heel (the back part) or above the ankles is not valid. This is because the ankle must be covered by the sock, and the wiping must be on the area that fulfills the requirement.

Key Terms
ظاهر الخف (zahir al-khuff): The outer (upper) surface of the leather sock, opposite to the sole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which part of the leather sock must be wiped according to the Hanafi school?
A) The inner surface (sole)
B) The outer surface (top)
C) Both equally
D) Any part that covers the foot

Key Takeaway
Wiping on the outer surface of the leather sock is obligatory; the inner surface, heel, and above the ankle are not valid areas for masḥ.

Minimum Amount of Wiping: Three Fingers
Specifies the minimum area of wipe: amount of three fingers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum area required for wiping over leather socks (mash) in the Hanafi school and distinguish the two views on the basis of measurement.

Core Idea
Wiping over leather socks requires covering an area equal to three fingers of the hand; less than that invalidates the wipe.

This passage specifies the minimum area that must be covered when wiping over leather socks (mash). It establishes that the wipe must cover an area equivalent to three fingers in length and width, and this applies independently to each foot. The text also highlights an internal Hanafi discussion about whether the three fingers are measured from the hand (the tool) or from the foot (the object), with the more correct view being the hand.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over leather socks (mash ala al-khuffayn). The ruling is that it is wajib to cover an area equivalent to three fingers of the hand in length and width on each foot.
The ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah.
2
Define the required measure
Three fingers refer to the area covered, not the exact fingers used. The area must be three fingers in length and three fingers in width, but the width of three fingers placed side by side is sufficient.
The measure is taken from the hand, not the foot, according to the correct view.
3
Note independence of each foot
The requirement applies to each foot separately. If one foot is wiped with less than three fingers, that wipe is invalid, even if the other foot is wiped adequately.
4
Recognize the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion on whether the measure is taken from the smallest fingers of the hand (as the wiping tool) or from the foot (as the place of wiping). Abu Bakr al-Razi and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad hold the hand measure; others analogize to head wiping.
The author prefers the hand measure.
5
Apply the preferred view
The more correct view (al-ashahh) is that the obligation is the amount of three fingers from the hand. It is permissible to wipe with three fingers placed together without stretching them out, as the requirement is the extent covered.
Mufta bihi: three fingers of the hand.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بثلاث أصابع: أي بقدر ثلاث أصابع اليد طولاً وعرضاً لكل رجل بالاستقلال، فلو مسح على واحدة بقدر إصبعين، وعلى الأخرى خمساً، أو على كل أقل من ثلاث لا يجوز في الصحيح، ثم لم يذكر محمد في "الأصل" أن التقدير بثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد اعتباراً بآلة المسح، أو أصابع الرجل اعتباراً محل المسح، وكان الفقيه أبو بكر الرازي يقول: التقدير بثلاثة أصابع اليد، وهو رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة، وفي "الكافي": الكلام فيه كالكلام في مسح الرأس، فمن شرط الربع ثمه شرطه ههنا أيضاً، ومن شرط أدنى ما يطلق عليه اسم المسح ثمه شرط هنا أيضاً، ولو مسح بثلاث أصابع موضوعة غير ممدودة جاز؛ لأن فرضه مقدار ثلاث أصابع من اليد، وهو الأصح. (مسكين وغيره)
'With three fingers': i.e., to the extent of three fingers of the hand in length and width, for each foot independently. So if one wipes on one foot with the extent of two fingers and on the other with five, or on each less than three, it is not valid in the correct view. Then Muhammad did not mention in al-Asl whether the estimation is by three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand, considering the instrument of wiping, or by the fingers of the foot considering the place of wiping. The jurist Abu Bakr al-Razi used to say: the estimation is by three fingers of the hand, and this is a transmission from al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa. In al-Kafi: the discussion here is like the discussion on wiping the head: whoever stipulates a quarter (of the head) stipulates it here also, and whoever stipulates the minimum of what is called 'mash' stipulates it here also. If one wipes with three fingers placed without stretching them out, it is permissible because the obligation is the amount of three fingers from the hand, and this is the more correct view. (Miskin and others)
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage addresses the minimum area required for valid wiping. The ruling is that the wiping must cover an area equivalent to three fingers (of the hand) in both length and width. This is for each sock independently, so wiping one sock with less than the equivalent of three fingers invalidates that sock's wipe, even if the other is adequate. The text mentions a difference of opinion within the school: Imam Muhammad did not specify in al-Asl whether the three fingers are taken from the smallest fingers of the hand (as the wiping tool) or from the toes (as the object). Abu Bakr al-Razi preferred the hand's fingers, and this is a transmission from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa. The analogy with wiping the head is mentioned: some scholars require at least a quarter of the head, and they apply the same here; others require the minimum that constitutes wiping linguistically. The more correct view (al-ashahh) according to the author is that the obligation is to wipe the amount of three fingers from the hand (not necessarily the smallest), and it is sufficient even if the three fingers are placed together without being spread out. This is because the requirement is about the extent covered, not about using exactly three fingers.

Key Terms
ثلاث أصابع (thalath asabi'): The minimum area of wiping: an area equivalent to three fingers of the hand in length and width.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum area that must be covered when wiping over leather socks according to the correct Hanafi view?
A) One finger
B) Two fingers
C) Three fingers
D) The entire sock

Key Takeaway
The minimum area for valid wiping over leather socks is the equivalent of three fingers of the hand on each foot.

Definition and Legal Status of Wiping over Leather Socks
Opens the chapter with definition, basis, and evidence for wiping over leather socks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mash 'ala al-khuffayn and explain its legal basis from the sunnah.

Core Idea
Wiping over leather socks is a confirmed sunnah of the Prophet, established by widespread reports, and a distinctive mark of Ahl al-Sunnah.

This chapter begins by placing wiping over leather socks after tayammum: both are substitutes, but tayammum replaces the entire body, while wiping replaces only washing the feet. The passage then defines the key terms and emphasizes that this practice is a distinctive feature of the ummah, citing Abu Hanifa's statement that it is part of the Sunni creed. The proof is drawn from the Prophet's actions and sayings, making it a well-established sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the placement after tayammum
Recognize that both tayammum and wiping are substitutes in purification, with tayammum being a complete substitute and wiping a partial one. This sets the context.
The link highlights the structural logic of the fiqh text.
2
Define the key terms: mash and khuff
Mash linguistically means passing the hand over something; technically, it is touching the wet hand to the khuff in the prescribed area. Khuff is a leather sock covering the ankle, suitable for travel or walking a farsakh.
The dual 'khuffayn' indicates that wiping on a single sock is invalid unless excused.
3
Identify the evidence from sunnah
The author cites the Prophet's actions (reported by many Companions) and his statement: 'A resident wipes for a day and a night, a traveler for three days and their nights.' This establishes the permissibility and duration.
The reports are so widespread that denying it is considered innovation.
4
Grasp the legal status
In the Hanafi school, wiping over leather socks is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed practice), not fard. It is a distinctive feature of this ummah and a necessary part of the Sunni way.
The hukm level is derived from the ahad hadiths, which give zanni thubut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المسح على الخفين: مناسبة هذا الباب بباب التيمم أن التيمم خلف عن الكل والمسح خلف عن البعض، والمسح على الخفين من خصائص الأمة. والمسح لغةً: إمرار اليد على الشيء، واصطلاحاً: إصابة اليد المبتلة الخف، أو ما يقوم مقامه في الموضع المخصوص في المدة الشرعية، والخف مأخوذ من الخفة؛ لأن الحكم خف به من الغسل إلى المسح، وهو شرعاً: ما يستر الكعب، أمكن السفر به أو السعي به فرسخاً، وفي التثنية إشعار بأنه لا يجوز المسح على خف واحد بلا عذر (فتح) وقال في "المستخلص : المسح على الخفين ثابت بالسنة المشهورة التي يجوز بها الزيادة على الكتاب، والأخبار فيه مستفيضة حتى قيل: إن من لم يره سنة يكون مبتدعاً؛ لما روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه سئل عن مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة، فقال: هو أن تفضّل الشيخين، وتحب الختنين، وترى المسح على الخفين. والمسح ثابت عن النبي ﷺ فعلا وقولاً، أما فعلا فقد روى أبو بكر وعمر والعبادلة الثلاثة وأبوهريرة وخديجة وعائشة رضي الله عنهم أنه عليه السلام مسح على خفيه، وأما قولاً: فما روى عمر وعلي وصفوان وعائشة رضي الله عنهم أنه عليه السلام قال: "يمسح المقيم يوماً وليلة والمسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها"، والأخبار فيه كثيرة. (ملخصا) ولو امرأة: أي ما لو كان الماسح امرأة؛ لعموم النص. (ط) لا جنباً : [ أي لا يصح إذا كان جنباً؛ لأنه لا يتأتى الاغتسال مع الخف الملبوس] معناه مما يوجب الغسل كالحيض والنفاس والدليل عليه حديث صفوان، فهو صحيح في منعه للجنابة، وهو ما ورد أنه عليها كان يأمرنا إذا كنا سفراً أن لا ننزع خفافنا ثلاثة أيام ولياليها لا عن جنابة، ولكن عن بول وغائط ونوم، وروي "إلا من جنابة" وكلاهما صحيح؛ ولأن الجنابة أو جبت غسل جميع البدن، ولا يتأتى الاغتسال مع الخف، ولما كان هذا الموضع موضع النفي فلا يحتاج إلى التصوير. وقال في "الكفاية": صورته: مسافر معه ماء توضأ ولبس الخفين، ثم أجنب وتيمم للجنابة، ثم أحدث ومعه ما يكفي للوضوء، لا يجوز له المسح على الخفين؛ لأن الجنابة سرت إلى القدمين، وذكر في "البدائع" أن جواز المسح في الحدث الأصغر لدفع الحرج؛ لأنه يتكرر والجنابة لا يغلب وجودها فلا يلحقه الحرج في النزع. (فتح، مستخلص) على وضوء تام [فلو تيمم ولبس ثم وجد الماء لا يمسح] احتراز عن وضوء غير مسبغ بأن بقي من أعضائه لمعة لم يصبها الماء، فأحدث قبل الاستيعاب، لا يجوز له المسح، وعن وضوء ناقص أيضاً بأي شيء كان نقصه كوضوء المستحاضة ومن بمعناها وكالمتيمم إذا لبس خفيه ثم وجد الماء، فإنهم لا يمسحون؛ لعدم اللبس على وضوء تام. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٨/١] تام فلو غسل رجليه أولا ولبس خفيه وأحدث قبل إتمام الوضوء لا يمسح. (ط)
Chapter on wiping over leather socks: The appropriateness of this chapter after the chapter on tayammum is that tayammum is a substitute for the whole (body), and wiping is a substitute for part. Wiping over leather socks is a distinctive feature of this ummah. Linguistically, 'mash' means passing the hand over something. Technically, it is: causing the wet hand to touch the khuff, or its equivalent, in the specific place within the prescribed period. 'Khuff' is derived from 'khiffah' (lightness) because the ruling was lightened from washing to wiping. Legally, it is: that which covers the ankle, and it is possible to journey with it or to walk a farsakh in it. The dual form indicates that wiping on a single sock is not allowed without an excuse (Fath). The author said in al-Mustakhlas: Wiping over leather socks is established by the famous sunnah by which addition to the Book is permitted, and the reports on it are widespread, to the extent that it is said that he who does not consider it sunnah is an innovator. This is because Abu Hanifa was asked about the way of Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah, and he said: It is that you prefer the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar), love the two sons-in-law (Uthman and Ali), and hold the view of wiping over leather socks. Wiping is established from the Prophet ﷺ both by action and speech. As for action, Abu Bakr, Umar, the three Abdallahs (Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Umar, Ibn Abbas), Abu Huraira, Khadija, and Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them) reported that he ﷺ wiped over his socks. As for speech, Umar, Ali, Safwan, and Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them) reported that he ﷺ said: 'A resident wipes for a day and a night, and a traveler for three days and their nights.' There are many reports on this. (Summarized) 'And even if a woman': i.e., even if the one wiping is a woman, due to the generality of the text. (T) 'Not in a state of janabah': [i.e., it is not valid if one is in janabah, because washing the entire body cannot be achieved while wearing socks.] Its meaning is that which necessitates ghusl, such as menstruation and postpartum bleeding. The evidence for this is the hadith of Safwan, which is authentic in prohibiting wiping for janabah. It is reported that he (the Prophet) used to command us, when we were traveling, not to remove our socks for three days and their nights, not due to janabah, but due to urine, feces, and sleep. It is also narrated as 'except from janabah,' and both are authentic. Also because janabah requires washing the entire body, and washing cannot be achieved while wearing socks. Since this is a negation, no illustration is needed. Al-Kifayah says: An example is a traveler who has water, performs wudu and puts on socks, then becomes junub and performs tayammum for janabah, then has an hadath while having enough water for wudu. He is not permitted to wipe over the socks because janabah extends to the feet. Al-Bada'i' mentions that the permissibility of wiping in minor hadath is to remove hardship because it recurs, whereas janabah does not frequently occur, so hardship in removing socks does not apply. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'On complete wudu' [If one performs tayammum and puts on socks, then finds water, he does not wipe.] This excludes an incomplete wudu, such as when a limb remains dry without water, and then he has an hadath before completing coverage; wiping is not permitted. Also an incomplete wudu of any kind, such as the wudu of a woman with chronic menstrual bleeding (istihadah) and the like, and the tayammum person who puts on socks then finds water; they do not wipe because the socks were not put on in a state of complete wudu. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 28/1] 'Complete': if he washes his feet first and puts on socks, then has an hadath before completing the wudu, he does not wipe. (T)
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on wiping over leather socks (mash 'ala al-khuffayn). It begins by explaining the placement of this chapter after tayammum: both are substitutes, but tayammum replaces the entire ablution while wiping replaces only the washing of the feet. The author then defines the key terms: 'mash' linguistically and technically, 'khuff' as a leather sock that covers the ankle and is suitable for travel or walking a farsakh. The dual 'khuffayn' indicates that wiping on a single sock is invalid without an excuse. The ruling is established by the famous sunnah, and the author emphasizes that it is a distinctive feature of this ummah, quoting Abu Hanifa's famous statement on the Sunni position. The proof is given through the hadith of Safwan and others. Then the conditions are stated: it is valid for women as well (due to generality of proofs), but not for a person in janabah (major impurity) because the obligation of ghusl cannot be fulfilled with socks on. The evidence is the hadith that permits wiping only for minor hadath (urine, feces, sleep) and explicitly excludes janabah. An example from al-Kifayah illustrates a scenario where a traveler becomes junub and then has minor hadath; he cannot wipe because his feet are considered impure from janabah. The final condition is that the socks must be put on after a complete wudu (tamam al-wudu). This means the wudu must be fully completed before putting on the socks. If one washes only the feet, puts on socks, then completes wudu but has an hadath before completion, wiping is invalid. Similarly, if wudu was incomplete (e.g., a dry spot), or if it was a wudu of a mustahadah (chronic blood) or the person performed tayammum first, then the condition is not met. The key principle: the socks provide protection from impurity reaching the feet only when they are put on in a state of purity.

Key Terms
المسح على الخفين (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn): The act of passing wet hands over leather socks as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
الخف (al-khuff): A leather sock that covers the ankle and is suitable for travel or walking a farsakh.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal status of wiping over leather socks in the Hanafi school?
A) Fard
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Wajib
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Wiping over leather socks is a confirmed sunnah established by the Prophet's action and speech, and a distinctive practice of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Conditions for Valid Wiping: Women, Janabah, and Complete Wudu
States the conditions for validity of wiping: includes women, excludes junub, and requires complete wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three conditions for valid wiping over leather socks and apply them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Wiping is valid for women, but invalid for one in janabah, and requires wearing socks after complete wudu.

After establishing the basis and definition, the passage turns to the conditions for the validity of wiping. The author states three key rulings: it is valid for women just as for men, it is not valid for a person in janabah (major impurity), and it requires that the socks be put on after a complete wudu. Each condition is supported by evidence and rationale.

Guided Path
1
Include women in the ruling
The phrase 'wa law imra'ah' clarifies that women are included in the permission to wipe. The evidence is the generality of the proofs (عموم النص), meaning the hadiths do not specify gender.
This refutes any misconception that wiping is only for men.
2
Exclude the state of janabah
The text states 'la junuban' – wiping is not valid for one in janabah. The evidence is the hadith of Safwan which permits wiping for minor hadath but explicitly excludes janabah. The rationale is that ghusl requires washing the entire body, which cannot be done with socks on.
Janabah includes menstruation and postpartum bleeding.
3
Ensure complete wudu before wearing socks
The condition 'ala wudu' tamm' means the socks must be put on after a complete wudu. If the wudu was incomplete (e.g., a dry spot), or if one performed tayammum first, or if one washed only the feet then put on socks before completing wudu, wiping is invalid.
The purpose is that the feet are pure at the time of wearing, so the socks protect them.

Definition and Proof of Wiping over Khuffs
Defines wiping over khuffs and provides its evidence from Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of masḥ and khuff, explain the conditions for its validity, and cite the primary evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is a confirmed Sunnah and a distinctive belief of Ahl al-Sunnah.

This lesson opens the chapter on wiping over khuffs, a unique dispensation for this ummah. The author defines the act, its object, and conditions, then provides overwhelming proof from the Prophet's actions and words. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly performing wuḍūʾ in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State that the chapter is about wiping (masḥ) over khuffs. The act is a substitute for washing the feet, and its ruling is sunnah muʾakkadah (confirmed Sunnah).
Denying its legitimacy is considered innovation (bidʿah).
2
Define the key terms
Explain the linguistic and technical definitions of masḥ and khuff. Recognize that the khuff must cover the ankle and be suitable for travel.
The dual form (khuffayn) indicates two khuffs are required unless an excuse.
3
List the conditions for valid wiping
Identify the explicit conditions: the khuffs must be put on after a complete wuḍūʾ, the person cannot be in a state of janābah, and the wiping is partial (not necessarily the entire khuff).
These conditions distinguish valid from invalid wiping.
4
Locate the evidence from Sunnah
Cite the mutawātir reports of the Prophet's actions (many Companions) and his words (the ḥadīth specifying the duration for resident and traveler).
The evidence is so strong that Abu Ḥanīfa made it a criterion of Ahl al-Sunnah.
5
Evaluate the strength of the proof
Note that the ḥadīth is of ṭhubūt ẓannī (probable transmission) but its meaning (dalālah) is clear; the abundance of reports raises it to the level of practical certainty.
Ḥanafīs accept it as binding, unlike some other schools that require stricter conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المسح على الخفين صح ولو امرأة لا جنبا إن لبسهما على وضوء تام، أي المسح عن البعض، باب المسح على الخفين: مناسبة هذا الباب بباب التيمم أن التيمم خلف عن الكل والمسح خلف والمسح على الخفين من خصائص الأمة. والمسح لغةً: إمرار اليد على الشيء، واصطلاحاً: إصابة اليد المبتلة الخف، أو ما قام مقامه في الموضع المخصوص في المدة الشرعية، والخف مأخوذ من الخفة؛ لأن الحكم خف به من الغسل إلى المسح، وهو شرعاً: ما يستر الكعب، أمكن السفر به أو السعي به فرسخاً، وفي التثنية إشعار بأنه لا يجوز المسح على خف واحد بلا عذر (فتح) وقال في "المستخلص : المسح على الخفين ثابت بالسنة المشهورة التي يجوز بها الزيادة على الكتاب، والأخبار فيه مستفيضة حتى قيل: إن من لم يره سنة يكون مبتدعاً؛ لما روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه سئل عن مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة، فقال: هو أن تفضّل الشيخين، وتحب الختنين، وترى المسح على الخفين. والمسح ثابت عن النبي فعلا وقولاً، أما فعلا فقد روى أبو بكر وعمر والعبادلة الثلاثة وأبوهريرة وخديجة وعائشة م وغيرهم أنه عليه مسح على خفيه، وأما قولاً: فما روى عمر وعلي وصفوان وعائشة له وغيرهم أنه عليه قال: "يمسح المقيم يوماً وليلة والمسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها"، والأخبار فيه كثيرة. (ملخصا)
Chapter of wiping over the two khuffs. It is valid even if a woman, not a junub, provided she put them on with a complete wudu, meaning wiping from some. The chapter of wiping over the two khuffs: The connection of this chapter to the chapter of tayammum is that tayammum is a substitute for the whole (washing) and wiping is a substitute. And wiping over the two khuffs is from the special characteristics of this ummah. Wiping linguistically: passing the hand over something. Technically: the touch of the moist hand to the khuff, or what stands in its place, on the specific place in the prescribed duration. The khuff is derived from lightness because the ruling is lightened from washing to wiping. Legally: it is what covers the ankle, such that travel is possible with it or walking a farsakh. And the dual form indicates that it is not permissible to wipe over one khuff without an excuse. (Fath) He said in al-Mustakhlas: Wiping over the two khuffs is established by the well-known Sunnah by which addition to the Book is allowed, and the reports on it are numerous such that it is said: Whoever does not consider it a Sunnah is an innovator. Because it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he was asked about the way of Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah, and he said: It is that you give precedence to the two shaykhs, love the two sons-in-law, and hold the view of wiping over the two khuffs. And wiping is established from the Prophet by action and speech. As for action: Abu Bakr, Umar, the three Abdallahs, Abu Hurayra, Khadijah, A'ishah, and others narrated that he wiped over his khuffs. As for speech: Umar, Ali, Safwan, A'ishah, and others narrated that he said: "The resident wipes for a day and a night, and the traveler for three days and their nights." And the reports on it are many. (Summarized)
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, opening the chapter on wiping over khuffs (Bāb al-Masḥ ʿalā al-Khuffayn). The author explicitly states the ruling: wiping is valid for a woman, but not for a person in a state of major ritual impurity (janābah), provided the khuffs were put on after a complete wuḍūʾ. The commentary then explains why this chapter follows tayammum: both are substitutes, but wiping is a partial substitute for washing only the feet, while tayammum substitutes for the entire body. Wiping over khuffs is a distinctive feature of the Muslim community, proven by numerous mutawātir-level reports. The definition of masḥ is given both linguistically (passing the hand) and technically (placing the moist hand on the khuff to a specific extent within a set time). The khuff itself is defined as a covering that reaches the ankles and is suitable for travel of at least one farsakh. The text emphasizes that wiping is established by the Sunnah, and Imam Abu Hanifa considered belief in its validity a criterion of Ahl al-Sunnah. Proofs are provided from both the Prophet's actions (reported by many Companions) and his words (the hadith limiting the duration).

Key Terms
مسح (masḥ): Placing the moist hand on the khuff (or its substitute) on the specific area within the prescribed duration.
خف (khuff): A foot covering that hides the ankle, suitable for walking a farsakh or traveling.
وضوء تام (wuḍūʾ tāmm): Complete ablution that includes washing both feet before wearing the khuffs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How long can a resident wipe over khuffs according to the hadith cited?
A) One day and one night
B) Three days and three nights
C) Until the khuff is removed
D) Only for the duration of wuḍūʾ

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a confirmed Sunnah with clear conditions and evidence, and it is a distinguishing practice of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Three Conditions for Wiping Over Khuffs
Explains conditions for wiping over khuffs with proof and reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the validity of wiping over khuffs and explain the evidence from the hadith of Safwan and the reasoning.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is valid only if wudu was complete, the wearer is not junub, and gender does not matter.

The Hanafi school outlines precise conditions for wiping over khuffs. This passage expands on the matn's ruling, clarifying that wiping is valid for women, invalid for the junub, and requires a complete wudu before wearing. Understanding these conditions prevents common errors and ensures the act is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
From the text, extract the three conditions for wiping: (1) the person may be a woman (gender is irrelevant), (2) the person must not be in a state of janabah, (3) the wudu before wearing must be complete (tāmm).
The condition for women is stated explicitly: 'wa law imra'atan' (even if a woman).
2
Analyze the evidence for the junub condition
The hadith of Safwan explicitly excludes janabah from the permission to wipe. The text cites both versions: 'not from janabah' and 'except from janabah'. Understand why janabah invalidates wiping: it necessitates washing the entire body, which cannot be done while wearing khuffs.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala) in prohibiting wiping for janabah.
3
Understand the reasoning (taʿlīl)
The text explains the wisdom: wiping for minor hadath is permitted to remove hardship because minor hadath occurs frequently. Janabah is rare, so there is no hardship in removing khuffs. Also, janabah spreads to the feet, so washing them is required.
This reasoning distinguishes between frequent and rare impurities.
4
Apply the condition of complete wudu
The condition 'on complete wudu' means the wudu must be fully completed before wearing. If one wears after tayammum, or if any part is left dry, or if one washes feet first then wears before completing wudu, the wiping is invalid. The text provides these examples.
The completeness is judged at the time of wearing, not at the time of wiping.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو امرأة: أي ما لو كان الماسح امرأة؛ لعموم النص. (ط) لا جنباً : [ أي لا يصح إذا كان جنباً؛ لأنه لا يتأتى الاغتسال مع الخف الملبوس] معناه مما يوجب الغسل كالحيض والنفاس والدليل عليه حديث صفوان، فهو صحيح في منعه للجنابة، وهو ما ورد أنه عليها كان يأمرنا إذا كنا سفراً أن لا ننزع خفافنا ثلاثة أيام ولياليها لا عن جنابة، ولكن عن بول وغائط ونوم، وروي "إلا من جنابة" وكلاهما صحيح؛ ولأن الجنابة أوجبت غسل جميع البدن، ولا يتأتى الاغتسال مع الخف، ولما كان هذا الموضع موضع النفي فلا يحتاج إلى التصوير. وقال في "الكفاية": صورته: مسافر معه ماء توضأ ولبس الخفين، ثم أجنب وتيمم للجنابة، ثم أحدث ومعه ما يكفي للوضوء، لا يجوز له المسح على الخفين؛ لأن الجنابة سرت إلى القدمين، وذكر في "البدائع" أن جواز المسح في الحدث الأصغر لدفع الحرج؛ لأنه يتكرر والجنابة لا يغلب وجودها فلا يلحقه الحرج في النزع. (فتح، مستخلص) على وضوء تام [فلو تيمم ولبس ثم وجد الماء لا يمسح] احتراز عن وضوء غير مسبغ بأن بقي من أعضائه لمعة لم يصبها الماء، فأحدث قبل الاستيعاب، لا يجوز له المسح، وعن وضوء ناقص أيضاً بأي شيء كان نقصه كوضوء المستحاضة ومن بمعناها وكالمتيمم إذا لبس خفيه ثم وجد الماء، فإنهم لا يمسحون؛ لعدم اللبس على وضوء تام. رمز الحقائق: ۲۸/۱] تام فلو غسل رجليه أولا ولبس خفيه وأحدث قبل إتمام الوضوء لا يمسح. (ط)
And if a woman: i.e., if the one wiping is a woman; due to the generality of the text. Not a junub: i.e., it is not valid if he is in a state of major ritual impurity, because performing a full bath is not possible while wearing the khuffs. The meaning is anything that necessitates a full bath, like menstruation and postnatal bleeding. The evidence for this is the hadith of Safwan, which is authentic in prohibiting it for janabah. It reports that he (the Prophet) used to command us when we were traveling not to remove our khuffs for three days and nights except from janabah, but from urine, feces, and sleep. It is also narrated as 'except from janabah'. Both are authentic. And because janabah necessitates washing the entire body, and that is not possible while wearing the khuffs. Since this is a negation, there is no need for a specific scenario. Al-Kifayah says: The scenario is: a traveler with water, he performed wudu and put on the khuffs, then he became junub and performed tayammum for janabah, then he had a minor hadath, and he has enough water for wudu—he is not allowed to wipe over the khuffs, because the janabah reached the feet. Al-Bada'i' states: The permissibility of wiping for minor hadath is to remove hardship because it occurs frequently; janabah does not occur often, so there is no hardship in removing (the khuffs). On complete wudu: So if he performed tayammum and put on (khuffs) then found water, he does not wipe. A precaution against an incomplete wudu, i.e., if some part of his limbs remained dry, and then he had a hadath before covering the whole, he is not allowed to wipe. Also against a deficient wudu in any way, like the wudu of a mustahadah and those like her, and the mutayammim who put on his khuffs then found water—they do not wipe because they did not put them on with complete wudu. So if he washed his feet first and put on his khuffs and then had a hadath before completing the wudu, he does not wipe.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed conditions for the validity of wiping over khuffs, expanding on the matn's ruling. The author explains each part: 'wa law imra'atan' (even if a woman) — wiping is valid for women because the texts are general and include them. 'La junban' (not in a state of janabah) — if one is junub, wiping is invalid because janabah requires a full body wash which cannot be done while wearing khuffs. The hadith of Safwan is cited, which explicitly excludes janabah from the permissible wiping period. The text also mentions the legal reasoning (taʿlīl): janabah is a major impurity that spreads to the feet, so wiping cannot substitute for washing them. The condition of 'complete wudu' (wuduʾ tāmm) is crucial: the wudu must be perfect, covering all limbs. If any part is missed (e.g., a dry spot), the wudu is incomplete and subsequent wiping is invalid. Similarly, if one wore khuffs after tayammum (dry ablution) and later finds water, the wudu is not considered complete because tayammum is a substitute that is only valid while water is unavailable. The text also addresses the scenario of a traveler who becomes junub, performs tayammum, then has a minor hadath; he cannot wipe because the janabah's effect on the feet remains. This demonstrates that the ruling is based on the principle of removing hardship (rafʿ al-ḥaraj): minor hadath is frequent, so wiping is easier, but janabah is rare, so removing khuffs for the bath is not overly burdensome.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): State of major ritual impurity requiring a full bath (ghusl), such as after sexual intercourse or ejaculation.
وضوء تام (wuḍūʾ tāmm): A complete and perfect ablution covering all limbs and without any deficiency or delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if a person wears khuffs after tayammum (instead of wudu) and later finds water?
A) He may continue wiping for the full duration.
B) He must remove the khuffs and wash his feet with water.
C) Tayammum is sufficient, so wiping is valid.
D) He can keep the khuffs on but must repeat wudu.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is only valid if the wudu before wearing was complete, the wearer is not in a state of major impurity, and gender is irrelevant.
